O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear children, I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, together with its fulfillment, and have made the end through its expositions and its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is very strong in our region and is completely foreign to it, the science is lost and cut off, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in the books of the ancients that the hands have changed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I want to enliven it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments, and other instruments of the work with the addition of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their shapes and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and their number, and the movement and the veins that move and those that rest, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, Hippocrates said that the name, with the name, is much, and with the work is little; and especially in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should be careful not to fall into error and kill people; just as I have often seen many of those who undertake this science and abandon themselves without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut an abscess of scrofulous sores on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took on the case of a duke from our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture there was a wound; and the surgeon, full of ignorance, tightened the fracture over the wound with tight bandages, and did not apply any liniment to the wound, and left it thus for a time; and he ordered the duke not to loosen it at all; and it remained so that the leg became completely swollen, and the foot, and the leg was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and hurried to come and loosen the leg; and when I had loosened it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But nonetheless, the corruption had already taken hold in the limb, and I could not cure it; and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who lanced an entrenched abscess, and then inflamed it further through the wrongness of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is full of melancholic humor, it is not appropriate to touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, my dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is to say, work where there is danger in many ways; and I will show you in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, you must guard yourself so that foolish surgeons cannot speak ill of you. Take up your tools with consideration, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you achieve success and are praised. Leave the dreadful diseases of severe illness; and remove the tools that make you fear, and be strong in yourself so that you may pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not undertake a serious illness unless you are called a foolish surgeon.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is on cauteries by fire and cauteries by sharp medicine, and this chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet; and of the forms of instruments, and the forgings of cautery, and of everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is on cutting and piercing, and on cupping and wounds, and on the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is arranged and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is on restoring dislocations and twisting, and similar things; and is arranged from the head down to the feet, and of the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help, and of harm, is the longest speech and subtlest science and a secret matter; and about this many wise men spoke, and agreed on this; and their words are of little use to me, for I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally in every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some argued that cautery is a great help; and others said the opposite: that cautery is not worth anything for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot illness by heat, nor by dryness; and the one who says the opposite claims that cautery provides great help for a hot and dry illness that comes upon people's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare a man's body and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be so on occasion through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And certainly, only those who have tried it, and who know through long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the circumstances and duration of the time; we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery combined with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not affect anything but the member that is diseased, and harms no other member except slightly.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines travel from one member to another, causing the diseased members greater difficulty in healing; and perhaps they kill the sick person.  Fire, by its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study I have put into the art, and it has been based on the truth of things; and therefore I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that lies within fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels illnesses from the body, as the philosopher said when demonstrating; now receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauteries should be performed, and chose springtime.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the resulting harm is subdued by the help of cautery; and especially if the cauteries are necessary for pains, fierce and hasty, which cannot wait for the time when greater harm might befall the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think about it, dear son, as the foolish do; for the illness that is cured by cautery has no return; and they say it so; but it is not as they think, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humours which are the cause of the pain, and is more valuable than medicine for the speed of its value, and for the virtue of its work and its dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And a possible thing is that the illness sometimes comes according to the complexion of the ill person and the location of the illness and its virtue; and superfluities gather within it through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are applied to a place where there are few superfluities and moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worthwhile after medicine, but their understanding is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer various cures for an illness and they are ineffective, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with a gold instrument is better than one of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the high nature of its substance; and they said that the cautery's place does not cause rot, but this is not true, because I have experienced it, and have found it to be true in some men; and gold cautery is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat a gold instrument, you cannot tell when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; and if you heat it too much, it will damage the instrument; and thus there are enough impediments.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use iron cautery, because we have found it more suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or, I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Of olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are good for moisture and cold in the brain, and there are two types used for a disease called "soda", and for many humours that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothaches and sore throats, and especially for all diseases that come from cold, like paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The method of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a dissolving medicine that purifies the head for three or four nights, according to the strength and age and the custom of the patient can bear; and then raise the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his lap; after that, place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers will go, it will bleed from the nose; then warm the cautery called "olivare", of which here is the method:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move it downwards while gradually squeezing your hand in a circular motion; then quickly lift your hand, and look at the spot to see if you can see the bone just slightly; and if you don't see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that, take a pinch of salt, put it in water and soak some cotton in it, and place it on the spot and leave it for three days; after that, put softened cotton in butter, and leave it on until the burning is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and therefore, this method helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these said that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery on for a long time, and press so hard that one removes a piece of bone as wide as a spindle that women use in their spindles, so that the humors may flow out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; then one should treat and stitch it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem to me to be entirely good, except in some people where there is a fear of pain; and I think I should leave it alone; for the shoulder is weakened by the continued evacuations of its nature, as we witness in other limbs; and even when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, the first type of cautery seems safer and gentler to me, and with this I achieve a sound and healthy result.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain afflicts the entire head and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie," and head cleansings, oils, and plasters; and if one applies the cautery as we have previously described, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be careful if the patient's shoulder is strong and not too cold; then cauterize slightly under the cautery we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, cauterize each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery on the spot called "vessels"; and that is the spot where cupping is applied; and be gentle so that you do not go down to the bone. The patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of that elsewhere. And the cauteries of the horns must be finer than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain arises in a part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head has been cleansed with purifying medicines, and the other treatments I described in the division of illnesses have been applied, and none of this helps: then apply cauteries according to two methods, that is to say, with sharp medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries with sharp medicine are done by taking a clove of garlic, removing the skin, and slicing it slightly on both sides, then cutting into the temple where the pain is located in a manner that allows you to place the clove of garlic under the skin. When it has been placed, bind it tightly and leave it in place for twelve hours. Then, remove it and take out the clove of garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days. Then apply a piece of cotton dipped in butter until it stops bleeding.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	Afterward, treat with ointments until healed; and if you wish, use some of the burning medicines I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery with iron is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery iron, of which the form is:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because its head is shaped like a closed ring where there is a slight bend, and a small appearance in the middle. Place it on the painful area, hold your hand and turn the iron slightly until half of the thickness of the skin is burned; remove your hand so the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and a large amount of blood will flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, place cotton in vinegar water and apply to the area for three days; then put cotton soaked in butter and then treat the area with ointment until healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "knife-shaped," use the whole point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	of a migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a migraine as we have previously discussed in the divisions of diseases, and it doesn't work, and you see that the previously mentioned cauteries of medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the cautery called "knife-shaped" until it is white; and thus mark the painful area with a line of half a finger in length, and remove your hand once, and make sure you don't cut the artery and don't go down to the bone; and be careful of the jaw, which moves when one chews, and the nerve does not look at what moves and that spasms do not affect the patient, and be wary of the flow of blood from the artery when it is cut, where cutting causes great fear, especially for those who do not understand and who are not students and experienced; and leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, apply the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of an artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has applied dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery that is called "point," of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then prick all around the diseased ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move slightly above the root of the ear after you have marked the spot; and there should be ten pricks around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torment that must be cured by cautery is only effective for those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses; and do not apply cautery to those that come from dryness and spasms of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torment caused by phlegm from dropsy and purges of the head and gargles, and that doesn't work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery on the apparent healthy part, and cauterize the head of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cautery on until half the core is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the scalpel we have described before, but it is slightly more subtle, and the knife should be slightly larger; then treat the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When the apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vassel" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large and potent pills to cleanse the brain; then bathe the patient's entire head and place a mustard plaster on the occiput, as described in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is thus healed, it is good; and if not, make three cauteries from the middle of the head, descending down to the neck, and let there be one span between each cautery; and treat it as the others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient is enduring, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat it until he is healed; and let the cauteries be called "olivare," as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed with powders and as we have said before; then bathe the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind, and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist, and the patient is enduring, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until most of the skin is burned, and remove your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and let the cauteries be called "olivare," as we said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use fire cauteries except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain with powders and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is severe and enduring the taking of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, make gargles and chewing movements, cleansing the brain often with good foods; then bathe the head in the middle, and make one cautery as we have said before, and one cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is severe and enduring, make cauteries as I have said to those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-like according to the way I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make one subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and the phlegm thick, then cauterize it with the same cauteries as we have described for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities decline into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him to drink something to cleanse the brain, according to what has been previously described in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After bathing the patient's head, then make a well-made linen bandage, like a circle, and place it on the head; and the patient sits crossed, and is held securely from all sides; then apply the liniment, and take melted butter from a mature berbis; and warm it over a moderate fire, so that the patient can bear it on their head; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with other good treatment, until he/she is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize it by making several punctures with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization softens the brain equally; and then apply cotton soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' water
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water comes first to the eyes, according to the signs I have described in the division, then begin and give the patient something that cleanses the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him/her sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, instruct him to lie back, and cauterize in the middle of the head, and apply two cauteries to the two temples if the flow of water is to both eyes, or one if it is to one; and cauterize all veins and arteries beneath the skull, with a cautery as long as the temple's width; and watch out for excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with the power you possess.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incisions the precautions on how to stop the bleeding; and sometimes one cauterizes or cuts beneath the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are long-standing and habitual, and are along or near the veins or arteries visible on the head's exterior; and one sees that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then apply the cautery I described at the beginning of the descending water in the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or cuts beneath the two bones; and if more is needed, cauterize wisely above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it is of no benefit, then give the patient three nights' worth of draughts; after that, wrap the head, and cauterize or cut in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, slightly beneath the hair; and beware of the artery, so you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish, make two cauteries above the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not leave your hand there except until the third part of the eyelid is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelids turn inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are applied in two ways: namely, with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in a suitable position; afterwards, draw a shape on the eyelid that resembles a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be beside the hairs; then place moistened cotton in egg white and mullein poultice on the eye, then heat the cautery with which this shape is drawn.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize the shape you have drawn little by little, many times, so that the part is burned; and the sign of the healing of the work is that you see the eyelid retracted, and the hairs lifted from the prick of the eye; then remove your hand and leave it like this for three days, then place moistened cotton in butter until the burning is gone; then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs grow and the eyelid is softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot as you did before; and if the hairs are removed, cauterize it until the eyelid is raised to its natural position, and is even, and the hairs no longer prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make a myrtle leaf shape from parchment; then take French soap and warm vinegar, one ounce each, and grind them together thoroughly; and do it quickly so that it doesn't cool, then spread it over the shape you made like a myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid; and if the patient is holding only one eye, then one should work on one, and if on both, the same; and place cotton moistened in egg white under the eye; and the patient's head should be in a suitable position, and place your index finger on the medicine, and press it slightly and move it every time the patient feels the medicine biting, for it bites like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the biting sensation has passed, wash the area and see if you see the eyelid raised as if it were raised by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medicine to the area where the medicine hasn't worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are in order; then place moistened cotton in butter until the burned area is healed, afterward treat the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to, be very careful in your work so that no medicine gets in the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the eyelid becomes soft afterward, and the hair pricks the eye, then reapply medicine to the area softened by the eyelid properly, as you did before; then treat it until it is healed; and this is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that human eyes vary in size and smallness, and according to this, your constraints should be; and the correct path should not be ignored by the one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must apply cautery to it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Tell the patient to place their head on your lap; and let the attendants hold their head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or lower; then put cotton soaked in egg white or in parsley juice over the eye; then heat the cautery, which is shaped like the head of a swallow's wing, or the cautery should be shaped like a tent; however, this one shaped like a swallow's wing is better suited for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press on the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus and dry it; and if it is closed, open it and remove the matter; then apply the hot cautery firmly, and hold your hand on the cautery to the part of the eye that is above the nose, to prevent harm; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and destroy it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you bring the cautery down to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, repeat the cautery once more, and again if necessary, and leave it for three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply an acrid corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what is written in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a type of cautery for a fistula that some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and open the area; then place in the fissure a small spatula, the shape of which is as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it is made to the size of a lead [piece]; and hold your hand or spatula firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so the molten lead does not run into his eye; and it is necessary that one put on the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or in water; the lead will burn the area of the fistula and heal it with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have described, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a puncture to the nose, and to bring the fistula back to the body of the nose to its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of the cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cracks appear in the lips, called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in the divisions, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small, knife-like cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it on those cracks until it reaches the bottom; after treatment, cover the area with a cerote until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat, or to the uvula, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after causing decay and rot and becoming old and turning into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does no good: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; after that, apply it to the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and the last part; and do so once or twice, after that treat it with what we have said in treatments until it is healed; and if it is healed like this, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	on the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicine and it is of no use, then place the patient's head in your lap; then heat the cautery, which will be described later, in such a way that you place a rod over the tooth; and quickly apply the hot cautery to it, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and repeat the application of the cautery as you wish; then the patient should fill their mouth with salty water, and rinse for an hour, and then spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was moving is fixed, and the softened gums are tightened, and the corrupt moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or true cold, and the remedies of medicine are of no use, then there is need for cautery in two ways: and cautery of butter and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is such that you take cow's butter, and put it in a small iron or copper spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and soak it in boiling butter, and quickly apply it to the aching tooth and hold it until it cools; and thus do it often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, and put it on the aching tooth, and put hot iron on it until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is such that you take a piece of iron or bronze, and it should be large enough that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, as its form will be shown later, and apply it to the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then remove the fire; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And apply cautery to whatever part you wish, and according to your ability; and this is the form of the cautery iron:
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as its shape will be shown later, and let it have two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side of the cautery; and apply the hot cautery to the abscess once, or as needed, until it reaches the base of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is gone; afterwards treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the iron:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture overcomes the channels of the lungs, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be purged by dissolving medicines; afterward, cauterize at the root of the throat, but be careful not to go all the way down to the throat, and do not burn the heart but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, apply another cautery to the joint of the neck and the top of the spine, using a cautery called "clavile," of which we have the shape before; and treat the area as we have previously described until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When cough and lung ailments are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is old, apply two cauteries on the ribs in empty spaces; and one more cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be "clavile" according to the form previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you wish, apply cautery by pricking all over the cautery that is called "poins," of which the form is shown previously in the illness of the ears; and let the pricks be up to thirty, or as many as needed.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, treat the area according to what has been previously described, and let the cauteries be in three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this, the cauteries are lighter, because you make three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, let the patient lie on their back and on their side; then, lift the muscle which is within the shoulder joint with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inward, heat the cautery which has two nerves, of which here is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the muscle until it pierces the bone, and the figure of the cautery would be together with four cauteries; and because of this, a cautery with three nerves is made, so that the figure of the cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are like the thinness of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery with three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes one nerve is added to this, so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, put the cautery on the bruised area with a bandage; afterwards, let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upward, which rarely happens, then cauterize on the thick part of the clavicle bone, or a number of cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come into the stomach, so that it is not restored to its constitution, and catarrhs multiply in him, and with accustomed methods of treatment, he gains no benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back, and extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Thereafter, apply three cauteries: one under the breastbone to the depth of a finger, one across the entire clavicle, and two on the outside of the two ribs, so that the pattern of the cauteries forms a three-angled figure, and have such spacing between them that they do not join together when they discharge pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach the two sides of the heart, and the pattern of the cauteries be according to this form without joining:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and whoever fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and mark on the stomach that point according to the amount that you wish to mark; then cauterize with the entire cautery called "prick.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the ailment that we have had before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers pain from cold, moisture, and a large wind, such that it is driven from its natural constitution by superfluities; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, and it does him no good, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back; and mark three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this amount on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come; and have a space of one finger's width between each cautery; and let the cauteries be the length of the body, and do not press your hand too hard on the entire cautery; and let only half of the heart be burned, and let the patient stand upright on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you desire, cauterize these cauteries with the cautery-knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the entire heart, for you would dry up the whole body; and that it does not reach the boil, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and you know it to be so.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too severe; and if it is in the membrane, he feels violent pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment should apply to the sores, it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back; and then mark the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that is similar to a ray, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the heart is burned, and it comes to a scab, until the sore is completely gone; after the treatment according to the treatment of sores until it is healed; and it is not fitting that anyone but those who have long studied the art of medicine and by whose hands these diseases have sometimes been treated should use this cautery.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may confidently work, and nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to let it be.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Concerning the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should apply cauteries of aristolochia root to pleurisy, in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and heat it in the fire, and apply a cautery between the clavicle and the collarbone, and two small cauteries a little further down in the part below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly back; and one cautery in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand down, but act lightly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient authorities said that some men use a cautery of iron, resembling a razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and the pain departs, as we have said concerning the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this practice, there is a fear that the patient might die now, or a fistula might result that cannot be cured.
de la mice	Of mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice, according to what we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help, then three types of cauteries are appropriate.
