Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one way is that you make three or four cauteries, by following the length of the mice, according to the shape of the cautery of the liver that we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient often lie on his back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is at the location of the mice, where the patient's ribs come towards the left, and the lifting should be done along the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, put the two inflamed nerves so that the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and in this way there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize with the entire cautery with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment, when it has shed pus for a long time, and this is worth more than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is of no value for a person with dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in the divisions, and your treatment does not help at all, then you must make four cauteries around the abdomen, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one on the breast; and the cauteries should be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to shed pus for a long time, and do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be combined with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the clavile that we have shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been stated previously.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is hydrops, and are full of yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the ring finger and the little finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep, so that the yellow water would be expelled, and the cautery should be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the shin; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without curing, so that the water comes out; afterwards, treat it with the other cures that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the stomach ailment comes from cold and moisture, such that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened and cannot be cured by ordinary methods; and you see the patient enduring considerable suffering and of strong constitution, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what was said before in the cautery of the stomach, in a circular manner; and four cauteries around the navel, each one a small, subtle cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach next to the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and of large, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have described in divisions, but are still ineffective, then apply cauteries: three on the spine of the back, one close to the outside of the spine, small and gradually increasing in size and triangular in shape, and one cautery below the navel two fingers wide; and if you suspect that the stomach is cold, that the food does not digest, and that the face is swelling, then make one large cautery on the stomach, as previously described, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen, all small, subtle cauteries, and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure, treat the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshiness that is called "thelul".
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thelul, heat the cautery that resembles a scraper, and then place it, all burning, on the cut thelul; and leave it there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each part as we have said; afterward, treat with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize a large cautery on the skin, it will provide greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of a wound poorly cured.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will describe in its place, such an illness comes that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula occurs on someone, and is old and casts out putrid matter and corrupted moisture, you should probe it with a very thin probe and take care to know the probe's full depth.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Afterwards, heat the cautery that resembles a scraper, and insert it into the fistula according to the amount the probe entered, and repeat the cautery until the putrid and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the amount it needs; and be careful not to burn the nerves which are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder and the intestines, be careful of those places, and only make these burns in fleshy areas, and be sure that it doesn't go through; after treating the area until it is healed, and if the area is sealed, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter is not removed, know that the area is open, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted; and in the manner as one of these that we will explain in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and does not take the form of a woman's illness, then it is necessary for you to apply cautery to the kidneys on either side, using the clavile cautery we have previously described; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have three cauteries in a line, and greater assistance will be achieved.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then apply cautery to the outer part of the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the blade of a finger; and apply one cautery on the outside of the back, or two if needed; and the cauteries should be clavile according to the previously described form.
de la marris	Of the liver
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the liver is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers [i.e., fruits or offspring] are corrupt and their ends delayed; and when they come, there is great pain. Then it is necessary that three cauteries be applied around the loins, as we have said in the cautery for the bladder, and two cauteries on the outside of the back; and the cauteries should be clavile, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the socket of the hip, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the space of the separation is found empty, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip socket with one cautery in the shape of a circle, and mark it in front of the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and the cautery should be like that used for cauterizing the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip socket, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment is not working, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of the thick humours with fetid pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, apply cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, together burning medicines, and cautery with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many methods, of which one is this: you cauterize on the hip socket three triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make them well and deeply, and have the space between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cautery is applied in the middle on the head of the hip, so that there are four of them according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned regarding hip dislocation; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire hip, and all the thick parts of the flesh are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain is in the hip, and does not reach down to the thigh or to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it extends down to the thigh and leg, apply two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, slightly to the left side; and let the cauteries be in a knife-like shape, and let the thick parts of the flesh be burned; and if the patient feels the pain extending to the toes or near the foot, cauterize it there with three or four points using the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, apply more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, apply a cautery using the knife-like or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and major arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have applied cauteries to the ankle of the foot, and left them on so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the foot as well, and the entire foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly, from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cauteries to each, following this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said concerning the cautery of the hip, that this is the method: make an iron implement like this and let it be at the head as thick as a fingertip, or a little less, and be in intervals, and be from one interval to the other the space of a finger's breadth; and let the intervals be opposite on two sides, and be also like knots, and let there be a good handle of iron; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then place it on the affected hip joint, and let it be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize it once, then leave it for three days; and then apply a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment with ointment, until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we rarely use this cautery due to the fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and yet this is a good cautery for those who can endure it, and in the places where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you make an instrument with intervals, in which the margin of the opening descends, and it is of bronze or iron, with a long side, and it has two notches, and there is between each the thickness of a finger; and they are open in front and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After that, place it on the patient's hip joint, lying on their healthy side, and press your hand firmly on the hip joint; then pour between the two circles of warm water, which has been heated a little in the fire, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is burning like fire there; and when the burning is over, remove your hand with the instrument and wash the hip with soft water, and leave it thus for three days, and apply butter until that which is black from the burning is removed; and leave it three days for the rot to come out; and that would be the final aid after treatment with ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends down to the thigh or to the leg, then make an instrument that holds water according to what you have done for the hip likewise; and this is the manner of hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Make a small hole in it, so that the point of a razor can enter; and place another pot, well sealed, over that pot, and put alkali and lime and soft water over them, until there is a finger's breadth of water above the powders, when you have grasped it firmly in your hand; and leave it like this until water drips and falls into the sealed pot; then take all that water and pour it over the lime and alkali, as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very thin and is used in many medicinal works and in cauterizations of other limbs. For it acts like fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hip, such as turpentine, honey, and myrrh, and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen recounts a cure with which a man was healed of pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and praises it greatly, and says that no other treatment was given, and that he was healed in a single instance once this cure had been carried out, and that he had bathed according to what he teaches afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And says in this way, that you take fresh, dry green litharge, and grind it much with a little grease, and apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours, and in the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put him into a bath until his body is slightly warmed, and put him into bed, and the pain will leave entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps much; and the cauteries should be made in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe and the other, which is called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards, take dry goat's dung, and heat it in fire until it is embers, and put it on the wool, and let it remain until it is extinguished; and do this again, and do not cease to do so until you believe by feeling that it has reached the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "goat's cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from impact or from too great an evacuation, or from a similar spread of cold matter, no cautery is of value in any of these cases except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has been emptied of foul pills or similar things, that three lines of incisions be made on the back, where the pain is located, and on each line five cauteries, or more, according to the strength and the amount that the patient can endure; and the cauteries should be performed according to the cautery that is called "points"; and if you wish, make 3 or 4 cauteries on the middle, claviform cautery according to this shape:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight, narrow back when they rise, and fear; and you find the pain in the spine of the back and in those parts where other aches appear.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this shape.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery encompasses each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a piercing cautery of two or three lines, and let the points be close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterward, treat the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to any swelling that involves nerve tissue.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is caused by moisture spreading throughout the body's limbs, and when pain occurs in the feet, which the physicians properly call "podagra," and when it is of a cold nature and cures with medicines cannot remedy it, it is treated with cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it needs to be, cauterize above the sole of the foot, and apply cautery in the manner called "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains reach the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, put three or four cauteries on each knee, each one olive-shaped; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand over them any longer than is needed for the skin to be burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and the back, administer the cautery that we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks around the wrist two lines apart; and if any pain remains in the fingers, make pricks on each joint and on the skin of the hand; and if the pains reach the elbows or the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and administer medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge phlegm, he will be healthy by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the surface
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is recent, then when you wish to treat it, he should not eat that day; and he should use things that loosen the bowels, so that the stool descends from his belly; afterward, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are repaired, and bring them back to your fingers, and make a cut beneath the rupture on the bone of the groin, and make a mark that is like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and it throws sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then return the bowels to their place; and let the attendant hold his hand over them so they do not return back; and open the patient's thighs well, and place a cushion underneath him and a servant on the thighs, and another on the chest holding his hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your whole hand, and hold it firmly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you reach the bone; and be careful to prevent the bowels from jumping out when applying the cautery; so that you do not burn him, and that the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and for adults as large according to their size; after three days, treat the cautery area with butter until the burning is gone; afterwards, treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his nutrition be light for a long time, so that the bowels do not jump out when he moves around in the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, let the attendant provide him with a well-made bandage, and keep it on for 40 more days; and let him have good rest, let him work little, and avoid over-filling with drink and food, and excessive exertion; and when he follows these instructions, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment of cutting in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other parts of the abdomen and are recognized, and you want them to stop growing, apply a cautery of cautery according to its size, and let a third of the core be burned; afterwards, treat it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the location and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside it, and place your hand in the middle of the cautery and then apply it evenly.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then it must be cauterized with a cautery called "points", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, repeat another cautery on that one, for such is the custom that it must move to the limb that is nearest, wherefore it is necessary for you to do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Leprosy is sometimes helped by cautery, especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it to be cauterized, be wary if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend nor remain, and you fear that the corruption will take hold of the entire patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and keep your hand there until the cauteries reach the bone, and until the skin comes off so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize over the sores according to what is described above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the leprosy is spread everywhere; and it is visibly worsening, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have described on the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and another next to it, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are under the heel of the back, lest you burn them; and sometimes one makes a cautery on the bone of the fist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more help you give, and the more benefit; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And the cauteries should be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the forms of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, apply a mixture of flour, vinegar, with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size and smallness; and let the cauteries be slightly penetrating into the depth of the flesh; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand, foot, and back, at the point where the nerve that moves the limb, and in this way the swelling is removed; and nonetheless, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the points of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become advanced, and the remedies of medicine are of no value, then cauterize it with a cautery slightly deep, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed; then treat it with flour of vinegar and lentils, with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a colon and blood of an almond, each a portion; and mix them all together, and bind it with a cloth, and keep it exposed to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a sore appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet wise men say that one should also cauterize the middle of the sore; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen on some occasions; and a more proper thing is that it be cauterized around it, with the cautery called "circle," as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati," and it delays healing, either because of the excess it causes or because of the age of the sick person, if they are decrepit (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of the time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterward, leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the whole cautery, then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them outside in such a manner that the course of the decay is eased.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of illness called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a consuming of the limbs, for it eats the limbs just as fire eats dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the illness is; afterwards, cauterize from all sides until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it three days, and apply to the cauterized areas a soothing poultice with oil until the heat of the fire is removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment with ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this illness is sometimes treated with sharp medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already described the treatment with sharp medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the sores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that on the feet, from outside, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large, foul-smelling thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cautery by fire, and cautery by hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cauterization by fire is done by heating a cautery, shaped like a roofing tile, made of good iron, sized to fit around the nail from all sides and having thin edges; then place it hot onto the nail, and rotate your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; leave it like this for three days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and apply the poultice overnight, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with a healing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are spreading outwards from the body, which happens often on hands and feet, then you must apply cautery with hot water; and it is done this way: take a copper or iron rod, or a roofing tile, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is to say, similar warts; and place the rod over it so that it completely surrounds it, then pour a little hot water on it, and hold your hand tightly, and press your hand while rotating so that the edges of the rod reach the root of the nail and can allow the hot water to penetrate deep to the root; and let the patient endure the slight burning from the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will be uprooted completely from its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after another until you remove all those that are on the body, then treat them with healing ointments.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold nerves, or from a quartan fever or other, you must make four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling, and hasten the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Of/Concerning/Regarding the foul pustules.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes foul pustules appear on the body, which come from corrupted, thick matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If they appear, you must immediately apply a cautery to each head of the pustule: a thin cautery of myrtle wood, whose point is heated in the fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluities from which they came are broken up, and they are healed; but this must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are large flows of blood from the artery that is cut in the external wound, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very serious thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it firmly until the blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no more drops issue; then put several small and large olive cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either large or small, according to the wound and the location where the artery is severed, and place the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you remove your finger from above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another cautery from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes upon the sick person; and know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be well stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not pulled, or by a strong binding of thread, or by medicines applied which have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and pressed at the outset.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a remedy of tightly binding with cloths or applying burning things, or other similar things, will not profit much.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a mirror or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press it firmly until it is stopped on the wound and on the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often, so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed, thickened, and stopped; and subsequently do what is needed for cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the illnesses in which fire cautery or burning medicines are necessary, and the causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have arranged that chapter from head to foot, and I will follow the same path in this chapter so that one can find more easily what one seeks.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, my dear son, you must understand that this chapter has more peril and fear than the first one on cauteries, and therefore more caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and in incising an abscess, and in treating wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	For there come such who become so enraged with their illness that they die easily because of the frenzy they find in their sickness, and because of the great severity of their illness; and one must fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not agree with those who come to you with this manner, but put more regard on your honor than on your greed, and do not work foolishly but wisely with those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can receive praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most dear son, Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and may He inspire you with the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter, following the chapters that came before, or the chapter on cauteries, which I have explained from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	From a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children during childbirth, and when the midwife squeezes the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and in all those I have seen, death was swift; and therefore, it seems to me that it is better to leave this type of treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture increased until it died, and this moisture has gathered under the bone on the surface, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is like this if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you split a wide fissure in the middle of the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, as long as the moisture runs; and see here the form of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscess is larger, then make two fissures in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs you see are the sutures of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not answered: then you must split the head into three fissures according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture outwards.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, bind the fissures with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head heal evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strong and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look at where the abscess is large, and the collection of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess and the collection of water are visible, and slit it as much as you can; and be careful not to cut an artery; and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone suffers a disease called "catarrh" in their eyes or chest, and the illness is long-standing, and the treatment of medicine is of no use, then the final cure is cauterization, where the two arteries will be cut.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, when you are about to cut them, that the patient lean back their head; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient tightly wraps a cloth around their neck; then check where the veins are, and the locations of each are behind the ears, and they are slightly visible; then mark the spots, and cut each with a sharp scalpel from both sides, so that the cut reaches the bone, and it should be close to the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, place the scalpel under the artery and cut above it, while cutting through as you ought.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will spurt out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery is not visible to the touch, you must measure the space of three fingers' width, then mark it, and cut down to the bone; and what is necessary of blood to be released is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure and the fullness of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains on the bone a slight trace of the surface, cut it so that no further abscesses develop, then bind the wound and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of the tears and heat in the temples and other chronic madness and similar things, and if he is medicated by various medical treatments and none of it benefits him, we will extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls back the hair from their temples, and locate the artery that appears in the temple, for it is clearly visible by its pulsation, and it is rarely exposed except in some men who are very cold; and if it is exposed, the patient should bind its neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and apply hot water to the area until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula, of which the form is:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then gently scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues beneath it on each side; and if the artery is small, you should turn it with the tip of a hook, and then cut that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not completely stop flowing.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from six ounces to three; and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that no putrefaction occurs before the wound is closed, and bleeding occurs; then cut the excess that is between the two ties at that same time, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a knife cautery to the bone until the edges are cut; and this is the most effective method if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are a remedy for ending moisture; therefore, they are more helpful for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For in the extraction of arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place well-made bandages over it; and when they are removed, it should be treated with dry medicines that promote the growth of tissue and bandages until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery while you work on it, hasten to cut it with a cautery, or fill the area with vitriol and hold it with your hand to stop the bleeding; and if you do not have that, place your finger over the area until the blood is clotted, and rinse the area with cold water until the blood stops, and it is held as necessary; and the best and easiest way to extract the artery is to cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery from both sides, but the cuts should be wide to maintain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one finger's breadth of space between the two blades, and then, when you have marked the two places, you put the burning iron on top until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be spaced apart, for it is not completely fused with this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes are flowing down the veins on the top of the head, and no treatment with medicine is helping, and you see the patient's face becoming red, and feel trembling or shivers on the forehead; and the skin is thin and moist, so that the hair on the temples has fallen out, and the temples are burning and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
