Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "contused cure," and it is done to the patient suffering from this illness, by removing the hair from their forehead, then making three equal incisions on the forehead, along the length of the forehead; one incision should be about two fingers' width in the center of the forehead, going down towards the nose; the other two incisions should be on either side of the temples, and be careful not to cut the arteries on either side of the temples; keep your hand away from the area near the two jawbones. Each incision should be about three fingers' width apart and be joined together; have a piece of sponge and some cloths ready to wipe away the blood; then apply a pointed spatula from two sides, following this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision next to the temple down to the second incision; and burn all the flesh between the two incisions, on the entire surface above the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one; then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert the instrument called a "cultellaire" into the first incision; it is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side of it towards the flesh and skin, and the smooth side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, until the incision is continuous down to the flesh, and then do the same in the middle incision down to the other end; and then drain the blood, and cleanse the area where the blood was taken; then put a piece of old cotton into each incision, and place wet cloths in wine, oil, and vinegar, and be careful that no hot abscesses appear there; on the third day remove the bandage and administer a lot of hot water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil and other remedies for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of the cold in the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some people get an acute cold, and you see their eyes swollen and small, and their vision impaired, and their eyelids inflamed; and their hair falls out, and there is sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then you know by these symptoms that the material and cold come from many veins, and the best treatment is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you order the patient to lie on their back, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another one the width of the letter I.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the incision, and place old cotton and linen strips there; then apply cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful of a hot abscess; when removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, and then treat with things that cause drying, which make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or a beast, or a mineral stone or something similar, like iron; or seed, like peas, beans, or lentils; or a flowing substance, like water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other thing falls into the ear that does not join with the ear, nor grow within the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distil a small amount of violet oil or sesame oil, then apply it for extraction; and make him sneeze with a condiment, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and raise the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often, pus comes out with this treatment; and if it does not come out, apply extraction with fine tweezers, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with the tweezers, it is good; if not, apply extraction with a fine, small double-ended hook; and if it does not come out with this, make a small copper wire and push the end of the wire into the opening of the ear firmly, and cover what is around the wire with softened wax so that the wind cannot enter with the wire; then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take glue with which birds are caught, and put in it a suitable instrument to do this, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue over the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all these things we have said, hurry to open the ear before a hot abscess and spasm comes, and the method of opening it is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and draw out blood according to the measure of their strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty or dependent area; and let the incision be like a crescent, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and quickly suck it into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain inside and it swells, apply extraction; and if it cannot come out, apply a fine, thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is swollen due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water, then, that falls into the ear, the patient must first use a sneezing remedy, and clean the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaps out through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many stones, according to the length of your thumb, and light, and warm them a little in the fire; and let the patient put one or a few in their ear, and leap on it with their feet on the other side, and place another stone on the stone in the ear; and do not cease to do this, stone on stone, until the water goes completely out, and thus it leaps completely out; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and hold the other end over fire until the most delicate part of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until the water goes out completely, as we have said in the case of the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the creature, if it is of small body, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body that one can feel it, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In extracting worms lodged in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not profit at all, you must examine the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, extract them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the rod of which the form is here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the finest end into the ear, according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then suck firmly on the entire rod; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, stuff around the rod with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not leap out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which the form is here as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or bronze, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distilling; and to press the distillation inside, use a well-made bronze instrument for this; and if you want, take a scraper and wrap cotton around its tip; then put your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you want, into the rod, and the rod should be in the ear; then put the scraper inside all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or dripped out of the ear; and the patient should smell it inside, and the distillations should be slightly warmed by fire before distilling it into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to adults through the blockage of a wound, or of flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is a slight protrusion of the hole, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which goes deep, so that one cannot see it, is a difficult ailment in many dispositions, and for that which one can see, you must put the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage, then open it with this instrument of which the form is:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and cutting at the front and back, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is of flesh grown or in the cartilage of the ear, then hold it with delicate pincers and cut it slightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the blockage is deep inside the ear, then take a delicate, light scraper and warm it slightly in the fire, then place it in the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the blockage, of which the patient feels pain in hearing, pierce it slightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is closed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle crushed vitriol on it; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary to remove the tent and put another tent moistened with cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding that are used for treating discharges.
de la char des papieres	of the skin of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment, which comes from papers in the eyes when they are moist and dry, requires you to separate them with tweezers and forceps, and cut it with a scalpel from its roots; then put crushed vitriol on the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is worthwhile; and many times they recur, since some part remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there appear in the eyes things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called "grandine," and it is a collection of moisture thick in the eye membrane above and below; the work is as follows: be careful if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and that is an easy thing to know; then cut it broadly, then lightly peel it off each part, then take it with forceps and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the membrane a little, do not worry the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a stitch and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not exert force, for the ointment will restore it quickly and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, reverse the membrane, and grasp the grandine with forceps, cut it and press it from one side and the other; and if the membrane is detached by the incision, this does not hurt; and when the grandine is cut, wash the area with salty water and treat the place with something that generates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is generated in the membranes above the eyes, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it greatly pains their eyes, and they experience catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because tears well up in their eyes; and therefore they often lie on their faces and sleep on their backs, and their eye membranes under their eyebrows are wet because the swelling and appearance have covered the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient places their head in your lap; then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent-like circle according to the quantity of exinach in each part, then place it over it; and press with your fingers on either side, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make a small incision in the middle of the moisture in a straight line, not wider than the incision made in opening a vein; and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exinach; and in several ways the exinach flows from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then carefully remove it all with a piece of cloth tucked between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to go too deep into the incision, lest you reach the entire membrane all the way to the eye and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the incision, slightly enlarge the incision until it appears; then remove it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them over the area, and bind it tightly with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are those who grind stones and apply them to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms at the site, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the eyelids in addition to those natural to them, and they become aged, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases, such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and albugo, to the point of destroying the eyes.  And the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine, according to what is said beforehand in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle at the base of the hairs, and draw the thread over the eyelid, and bring it down to the blade; then cut into the area beneath the eyelid, below the excess hairs, and cut along the entire area, from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove the thread, and place a small pad of cotton and cloth beneath the eyelid; then draw a figure of a bandage over the eyelid, like the leaves of myrtle, although the shape must be proportionate to the extent of elevation required for the eyelid, as previously explained.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one needs to cut a significant portion of the eyelid, according to how softened it is; then cut along the entire area on the two lines that you marked, beginning at the large tear duct and going to the small one; and one of the cuts should be near the natural hairs, about the width of a root; then one inserts a lancet into one of the two angles of the wound, and then the wound is scraped clean; then the two edges are brought together by stitching with a needle and fine wool thread, and the blood is wiped away, and the excess thread is applied to the eyebrows with some sticky substance, if you wish to do so; and if not, do not worry about it; then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches with drying and constricting substances, for the eyelid recovers at the time of the wound closure and union, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is a safe procedure; and there is another method: and that is to draw a shape on the eyelid, such as the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, with three spaced incisions according to the form below:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above, in small equal portions, according to the form shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you lack the strength to hold the forceps, and the parts are not equal, then take a needle with thread and place it in the middle of the figure; and place another thread next to the large tear duct, and the second thread next to the small one, and join the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift the entire skin over which you have drawn, as we have described, and then bring the two edges of the wound together by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess develops from your incision, soothe it with ointments and similar softening remedies; and sometimes the hairs on the eyelid are inverted: then you should use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment for the corners is as follows: you must turn the eyelid and cut it as I have described, and then make two corners artificially, and two fine strips the same length as the eyelid and the width of the space; and cut at the two ends where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly onto what rises from the eyelid, and press the two corners firmly; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin that is pressed will die, become hard and rotten, so that it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and the eyelid is raised, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the shape of the two corners you will create according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is this: take a fine needle and thread it with soft, fine silk thread; then join the ends and tie them together delicately, and the threads should be a palm in length; then neatly arrange another fine silk thread in the groove and tie the thread ends; then place the patient's head on your lap; and let it be close to the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is a delicate and precise procedure; then insert the needle through the entire groove into the root of the added hair, and pierce the eyelid quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then pull the hair out to the groove, and place that hair, if there is one or two or three or more, into the groove; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs emerge completely from the groove in the eyelid along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the groove is pulled and the hairs do not emerge with it, you will pull the groove under the entire thread you have arranged, until the groove emerges from the opening above and you can see it through the eye's vision; then pull out the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in place and the flesh grows; and if the hairs are small, attach a long hair from natural eyebrows, and leave it attached to it until it grows long, and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati" or rot, comes to the eye, it has two types: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through wounding, or cuts, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is that you split the wound, and separate the edges, and place linen dressings inside, and bind it until it is healed; and you should not use things that dry and restrain in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and water or cooked linseed and diaquilon ointment melted in some oil, and wrap it in a dressing, and treat it with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must guard against it uniting in the same way as before; and these treatments we have described are only for preventing this disease from returning in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the membrane that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is beneath, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental form comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way to treat it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and pierce it from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at two points in the flesh; then stretch the flesh over the needle, and cut it with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the membrane returns to what is necessary, that is good; if not, take a scraper and place it in the cut, and turn the membrane, and make two cuts on the inside of the membrane; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you have made, and form an angle so that when they are joined, the shape is like the shape of a letter called an "I Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to how sharp its sides are beneath, of what surrounds the membrane, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a wool thread; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and dressings until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a cut, or a stitch, or a cauterization, you must make a full incision under the hairs of the membranes, according to what has been said before; then separate between the two edges with a dressing, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the ailment, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters devise instruments with all their power how to return the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary in terms of work and tools, in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	sudden tearing of the membrane
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this fusion occurs in such a way that the membrane above is fused with the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, you must then insert the tip of a scraper under the membrane and lift it; and stretch it with pincers, until you cut what is above with a fine spatula, which must not be too sharp or too sharp, so that the patient cannot endure the excessively sharp spatula injuring the eye; and make your incision, with which you peel off that union, gently, so that the membrane returns to its natural shape; and the entire union is healed, and sometimes they apply saline solution to the eye, and wash it with fresh water and with a compress; then place a linen dressing between the membrane and the eye, and put moist wool soaked in egg white over the eye; and after three days, use compresses and softening things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles hard skin, and another that is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, and when touched with iron and attempted to be removed with pincers, it cannot be; and both types begin near the large tear duct and grow gradually until they cover the entire vision, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; and you lift the membrane with your hand, then grasp the nail with small pliers and stretch it upward; then take a needle, and put a horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and a strong thread in it; and slightly double the point of the needle and insert it into the nail, and pierce it completely with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upward, and peel away all the hair from the side of the nail that touches the pupil and the silk along the hair to the root, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a fine spatula and small force, and leave the natural tissue of the tear duct, so that the flow of tears is not affected by the incision; and sometimes the nail is removed only with forceps and thread, as we have said; then it is peeled away completely with a gentle spatula, in a way that is described like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch and break the fleshy tissue and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision, apply a little bruised oil and a compress made of litharge to the eye, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this type of nail is often treated with medicines; and it grows, as I have explained in the division; and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye and take a small sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently remove the nail, and if you see that it diminishes and the flesh draws closer, distil a compress of litharge and red oxide and bruised oil from your mouth into the eye, and bandage the eye until the next day; then resume the same work, repeating it until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is anything contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the tear duct tissue causes great harm in the eye, grasp it with forceps, and cut off a part, not all of it, so that the tears do not come; then apply a red compress made of litharge to the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows, covering the pupil and pressing against the eyelids, resembling a pomegranate rose; and the procedure is that the patient places their head on your lap, then opens their eyes, and gather all that flesh with appropriate forceps, holding it firmly; then cut the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting with a razor until it is removed entirely, taking care not to injure the eye during the procedure; and the incision should be like the removal of the splinter, as demonstrated later in this chapter; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with bruised oil or apply red oxide and similar corrosive medicines, and place a bandage of egg-white over the eye, ensuring it protects against a hot abscess; and if anything remains, and the blood turns hot, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with remedies for treating hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and similarly treat any flesh growth of this type in the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must adapt the treatment for each eye, according to its natural and accidental conditions, and surgical interventions; and do not put your hand to any of these procedures until you see that the affected member can tolerate the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that are covering the eye, impede its function and weaken the eye over time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must examine if the eye, in which the splinter is present, is strong, and there is no other illness besides the splinter; then proceed as follows: tell the patient to place their head on your lap, then grasp those veins with forceps according to their skill, and let the forceps be small and double according to this pattern:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two forceps be positioned in a row according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then carefully remove those veins with forceps, and wipe the blood one hour after another, until you see the veins clear from the eye; and take care that you do not damage the eye with the points of the instruments, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not damage anything other than the veins; and when you have done this, instill into the eye green and red ointment to dispel the remnants of the splinter.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove everything in that hour, apply a soothing eye plaster and leave it for several days until the pain is relieved and ensure there is no hot abscess, then resume according to the previous method until it is healed; and this is the way to apply force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and burning sharp medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it where you must cut open the abscess where it should remain, and remove all the moisture, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, remove it with all the instruments, as described; and it is called "aspre chief", and is made of iron sharpened at one end, and pointed like a file, as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it over the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is closed, and flesh grows, and the body of the boil is closed, and it remains like this for 40 days, and it does not re-open or become an abscess, and no bad accidents occur, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other way but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: and it is that you expose the bone a second time with iron, and sharp medicines, and when it is exposed, take a drill according to this form, and let the iron head have three angles, and the shaft be narrowed to the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it because the air comes out if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the area with drying medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the area hardens, the matter goes into the nose; so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the eye's discharge
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no disturbance to the nose, nor any narrowing, you must bind the patient; then cleanse it, then apply leeches or cups without hurting to suck, then put over the eye a bandage made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and gum tragacanth, and then bind the eye, and the plaster over it with bandages and strips; and the way of the strips is that you take strips soft enough, and double each one in four, and then place one over the other according to the quantity the eye needs; then bind it tightly over a hard bandage, and reapply the leeches to suck without hurting; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bandage softens, you must bind it tightly; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye improving, it is good; if not, then reapply the plaster, strips, bandage, and leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the tearing of the tissue (or cloth)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear occurs in the tissue (or cloth), and it opens, and comes out from the papery parts like a resin grain, and is frightening to see; then if you wish to stitch it, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the affected part, down to the top, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the tear duct area; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle in place; then cut the double thread and tie a portion of the tissue around it, and bind it tightly, then remove the needle and apply wool soaked in egg white; and leave it until the thread comes out with the tissue, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the tissue on all sides with a cloth circle until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows significant protrusion, pierce it with a very thin spatula that penetrates deep into the eye, and drain the whitish moisture that makes the eye descend, and re-enter it quickly; then bind it tightly until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the swelling of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This ailment, called "alcunnati," is nothing more than a swelling in the eye, resembling a descending sharp point, yet it is not sharp; and the manner of its appearance and treatment is this: make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take the head in your hands on both sides and move it so you see the swelling come towards your eyes; then let it settle and not descend and let the light be clear, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is a sharp point, and if the swelling does not descend properly as we have stated.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then make the patient sit between your hands, take the thin spatula, and make a small incision on the cornea along the conjunctiva's connection with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, drop warm water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, into the eye, then treat it further until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the sharp points of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already discussed the appearances of sharp points in the division, and what is needed to pierce them; so operate according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and hold the healthy eye tightly; then place the eye's membrane in your left hand if the affected eye is the left, or in your right hand if it is the right; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the affected eye is left, or in your left hand if it is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown, about the width of a finger, in the white part of the eye near the tear duct, then skillfully push the "almagda" instrument, and turn your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel the almagda reach the empty space; and the length of the almagda's path should be equal to the distance between the pupil and the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; you will see the bone through the membrane, thanks to the clarity of the cornea, and you can move the instrument to where the sharp point is, and then push it out one way after the other.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the sharp point descends now, the patient will see in front of them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, if the sharp point rises a second time, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly embedded and no longer rises, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand little by little; and then put a little of gem-salt onto the point, and wash the eye with it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply bandages or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white to the eye, and bandage it to the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply a compress with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have excessively hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then insert the almagda, as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare a suitable bed for the patient, where he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and let him eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and let him be bandaged according to his condition for up to three days; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and you must not do this during or immediately after the incision, but you must delay it, because the point rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If a hot abscess comes, unbind the eye before the seventh day, and apply something that soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, unbind the eye and place a cloth over it to cover for some days, and let him be in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then let him leave the room little by little, and return to his condition; and know that no apprentice should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iraq, who told us that in his country people pierce an almagda, from which they draw out water, but nevertheless, I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the forms of the almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be of copper properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let their heads be of the same thinness, and the rear in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various extra flesh grows on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs; and some have flesh that is deeply embedded with a dusky color, and some have soft flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that flesh which is soft and not embedded, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and apply the forceps to that flesh, and pull it out; then cut what you can hold with a thin sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any remains that cannot be cut, open it with all the fine instruments gently so that nothing remains; and if it is without swelling, or a simple abscess, treat it as is appropriate; and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then apply a thin sharp knife to the nose and pour in wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens, and moisture flows down to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is flesh growing on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then you must put a piece of coarse linen thread, tied tightly in your hands, with an inch or less of space between each knot; and have the patient put the end of the thread into their nose with all their might, and pull while smelling, until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and many children do this in school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold one end coming from the nose in one hand, and the other end coming from the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other while holding the knots that are in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have broken down that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and dip the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment dissolves what remains of flesh; and then put a lead chain in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the way to use instruments to clean the nose, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or bronze, like an open lamp, like a chain, and the conduit likewise; and if you wish, make a closed chain, and let the instrument be full to purge the nose; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease called "telul" arises on the top of the nose, and grows and becomes large often, until it is a horrible sight to look at; and therefore you must cut it at the beginning, and remove it entirely, then put the cautery or burning medicine on the spot; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, watch out if it is hard, of a dark color, with poor scent: do not touch it with iron, because it is a festering abscess, because when it is cut sometimes, it brings great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be entirely cut, empty it and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and astringent things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come upon one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
