Therefore, when this happens to someone, check if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then bring the two edges together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, you must scorch all the parts of their edges until they bleed, then bring the two edges together with stitches, and bind it tightly, and sprinkle on top powder of dragon's blood and crushed incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of strong plaster or another healing plaster, and leave it until it heals by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is to bring the edges together: either with needles, as we have described in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have explained to you.
des apostemes des levres	Of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many people develop hard abscesses inside the lips, like grains of millet, small and large; then you must turn back the lips and make incisions on each one, and use forceps to remove it in each part; then fill the place after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped; and then wash it, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, extra flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; therefore, you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, and allow the pus or blood to drain; then place powdered vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders, on the area; and if that flesh grows back after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it will not return after cauterization; and these are the methods for using the instruments to cut.
des sordens	Of the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, hard, rough scabs gather at the roots of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, and spotted, such that the rot extends to the gums and the teeth are foul-smelling; then you must place the patient in your lap, with their head in your grip, and scrape away the scabs or any visible hard matter until nothing remains; and in this manner remove black spots, green spots, yellow stains, and other blemishes, until they are cleaned away; and if you remove all this at the first attempt, that is good; if not, repeat it again the second day and the third, until all is scraped away; and know that teeth require various forms of scraping instruments, as the craftsman will show you, for the scrapers used to clean between the teeth have a different shape than those used on the teeth themselves; and these forms, and others, should be available to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when treating a toothache, that you delay extraction as long as possible, for this should not be done; for it is a very high-risk procedure until the scraping is done without any reservation.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is insistent on extraction, you must be certain of the afflicted tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times, pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and the good tooth is pulled; however, the pain does not disappear by this, until the bad tooth is extracted, as we have indeed seen in such cases; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, you should make a deep incision all around the tooth to protect the gum from all sides.  Then gently grasp it with your fingers or fine pliers the first time, until it is loosened; then hold the pliers firmly, and hold the patient's head in your lap between your knees, keeping it steady so that it doesn't move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not readily come out, use one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, you must fill it with lint where the holes are, and carefully grasp it with pliers so it does not break when you pull; and you must very carefully work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it and leave a part of it, which will return to the patient with greater pain from the root than the initial pain.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to do as ignorant practitioners do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and do not achieve what we have described; but they sometimes cause greater illness through the remaining roots or by breaking the jawbone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, or vinegar and salt. And if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that is not sufficient, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one moves the teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have thick limbs so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be of well-forged iron, and toothed for holding the teeth.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, you must place cotton soaked in butter on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then apply the pliers called "algefri", which make the head look like a bird's beak; and let them be filed like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with all these pliers, you must expose the flesh all around the root, and apply the instrument called "althali", that is to say a pick, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out with this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which the shapes are shown below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are shown in the arrangement of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments should be strong so that they cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth; and also other instruments, which are not listed; and the skilled, subtle master finds his instrument for himself, according to what his work and the patient demonstrate to him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of others; and if one breaks the cart or other bones, where it could, one should look for the instruments necessary, as I have told you, and use the gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with suitable medicines; and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, remove it with this entire instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with its natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, you must know if the tooth is born after another tooth, and is not in the correct place, and cannot be filed or trimmed; then remove it; and if it is attached to the tooth, then take this instrument, of which this is the shape, and it resembles a small beak, and be of sharp, hardened iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days because of the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a file such as this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which needles are made; and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks; then smooth the end with any scraper; and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth ache
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth ache, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot bear to bite down, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and it is of no use; then you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and put it double between two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you wisely reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the wrapping until the place where you started, and restrain your hand subtly and wisely, until it does not move; and let your tie be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, assemble them, and tie them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, then restrain it with another thread; so it will remain and serve throughout its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the way to straighten two healthy teeth, and two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place, little by little, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes a tooth-shaped piece of cow's bone is made and placed where the missing one was, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of cutting the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament, which comes from under the tongue by nature, is born this way; or by an accident of a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth, and hold their head steady, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament of the tongue, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it is from the healing of a wound, then use a needle and cut this ligament widely; and be careful that the cut is not too deep, due to the artery underneath; and when you are finished, wash the area with rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and the patient should keep it there every night so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol to the area; and if the bleeding is excessive, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a dark, black or hard discoloration, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is tending towards pallor, and there is moisture, then insert a needle and split it with a sharp spatula, and clear it on both sides; and if the bleeding is excessive during your work, apply powdered vitriol until it stops, then return to your work until all the impurities are removed; then clean the area with vinegar and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils appear in the throat, called "godath," also properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them as we have stated in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if they are hard abscesses, small in sensation and dark in color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent bleeding; but let it ripen, and then you will open it, or it will break on its own; and if it is pale in color, and the root is small, prepare the instrument for cutting, but first see if the abscess is warm and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and let their head be in your sight, and let them open their mouth, and let the surgeon take it in their hands, and press the tongue below with the whole instrument, of which this is the form; and let it be of fine silver or brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the forceps and place it in the tonsil, and pull it firmly upward as much as you can; and pull out any matter with it, then cut it with the instrument, of which this is the form, which looks like a pair of pliers; and nevertheless the tips are bent, and one facing the other, and are very sharp, and are made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cut it with pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one tonsil, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, the patient gargles with hot, clear water, and if bleeding occurs, the patient gargles with water, or boiled pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then treat it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut those like the two tonsils as well.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed in her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the obstructed passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had swelled so much that it had forcefully pushed two veins through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly acted, and inserted a probe into one nostril, then pulled out a large portion of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterward I inserted the probe into the abscesses, and cut a portion, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into the abscess for a long time; and the abscess would swell again, and fill the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I incised it and cauterized it in her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left her, and I do not know what God did to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When mucus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen below, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the section, and the treatment is of no benefit, and you see that the inflamed abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and the one that is round, gathered, and not elongated; and it is sanguine or of a dusky color or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have described, its color and its length, you should make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention previously; then, insert the hook into the eye, and pull it downwards, and cut it with one of the two instruments I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural boundary; for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said regarding the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use a method of cauterization to alleviate the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is sharp, sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head on your breast, then press their tongue with the instrument we discussed in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize with a hot sharp iron, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and fill the end of this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there should be a small opening in the head where medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and place the instrument containing the medicine onto the eye; and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth, carrying the medicine inside, so that it does not go down the throat and injure it; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye, for half an hour, until you see it has become clear and the effects of the medicine are subsided; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, dip the cotton into the medicine, and place the instrument with the cotton onto the surrounding skin, until the cotton dries on the eye; and repeat this often, until the cauterization is complete, then allow it to dry, and it will fall off in four or five days. And if you need to re-apply the medicine cauterization, repeat it, and after cauterization, wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is better than incision, rather than cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and ysop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and add oil, and boil; and the pot should be made of strong earth, and within the pot there should be an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one end should be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the channel, until the eye is deadened; then repeat often, until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because several things can happen; and do not do this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put an egg white inside one end, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; because egg white does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and this is a good and safe treatment altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, bone or fish spines, or some other object, get stuck in the throat; so you should extract what you can see, and press the tongue toward the sun with the instrument, so that you see the object move; and whatever is hidden and remains in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out with the vomit; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out with the methods we have mentioned, take a lead instrument in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the tip raised upward; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that nothing gets stuck, or push the bone inside; it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, so that it moves where the object is stuck; push it downward, or pull it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the leech on the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the leech is treated, as I said in the division, by the treatment of medicine; and when this does not work, then look into the patient's throat using the sun, and then press the tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine pliers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not enough, take a thin chain, and place it in the patient's throat, then place a hot iron at the end of the chain, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is feverish all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with the hand often; and as soon as the leech senses the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I described for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot with glowing embers, and the bottom is covered with a perforated cover; and in that hole is the head of the instrument; then put your fumigation into it, and the patient should place the head of the chain in their mouth, and close the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes down to the leech; and the leech will fall immediately, and if it does not fall, restart the fumigation many times; and let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty and pungent things, and do not drink any water; and then it will be necessary for it to leave by this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one draws the leech, is, when one can see it, like bent tongs to enter the throat; and it should resemble the beak of a bird, and have roughened edges like a file, so that whatever it grabs, it cannot let go; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many types of abscesses exist, according to the remembrance of others in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two types, one in its own appearance, and in the moisture it contains.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is according to their locations on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of fleshy areas differ from those that appear in joints, and each has its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And some abscesses should not be pierced until the swelling is ripe according to its completion; and some that must be pierced when they are swollen, and do not mature according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess is near a joint, and one leaves it until it is rotten around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is next to a major limb, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main limb; or if it is next to the foundation, it is pierced before it is ripe; and you must not pierce a swollen abscess without complete digestion, except for one next to the foundation, so it does not rot deeply, lengthen inside, and form a fistula; and it cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for piercing a ripe abscess according to its completion, and that is when the pain subsides, the fever departs, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the calming and softening of the abscess head, and the other signs; and you should make the incision at the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be along the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally where there is no skin fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of its venom will be extended, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and the depth of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that should be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small openings in small abscesses; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where you must cut the core, and cut; when it has become like a flag, and is dormant, you must do as one does with boils: and there are some that are cut into three angles, and there are some where one cuts like a myrtle leaf, as abscesses of the armpits; and there are some where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those that have no head, like a soft superficial abscess, you must pierce completely; and it is necessary, when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not remove all the pus at that time, but remove a portion; then seal the abscess until the next day, then remove some more again; do this repeatedly, gradually, until all the pus comes out; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes trembles with the discharge of pus, so that the patient may perhaps die, and you do not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound, and examine if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a simple incision, apply linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you place a compress in each so that they touch one another; and if you have cut a portion of the skin in the abscess, and you have cleaned it around, you must fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if a bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and ease, and wet a cloth, and place it repeatedly on the bleeding spot.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and remedies, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the area where the abscess is is very sensitive, you must apply compresses and cloths moistened in warm wine and oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, you must apply compresses moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then undo the bandage, dry the abscess, and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must universally know in treating abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head has small abscesses, and there are various types that are like webs, just like the yolk of an egg, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty and others where there is moisture like pus; and there are others that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the incision is that you test with any instrument called an "entromissor," of which the shape will be shown afterward, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then pierce it from above along the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then cauterize without leaving any skin that contains the moisture, for it often returns when you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and that will run what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second and third days, until you know for sure that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains fat, then cut it along this shape, lengthwise; and place your forceps there, and cauterize it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to draw out the matter where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with the abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and treating it, as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting on a stony and moist abscess is easier, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses, in the head, contain no moisture, and this was the abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it, one would have inflicted a wound just as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, except those which come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, in order to allow the pus to exit; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses appear on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous sore is properly within its own area, just like a boil or an abscess in the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulous sores are various.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see to be well-disposed when touched, and have the color of the body, and are soft on all sides, and are not close to the nerves of the neck, nor the arteries, nor the channels, and are not deep; then you should cut it open above, and scrape it from every part, and spread the two sides of the wound open with forceps, if you need them, as we said concerning abscesses of the head; and draw it out little by little, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that the instrument is not too sharp or cutting, lest your hand slip and go too far, and you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this hinders your work, then put powdered vitriol or other powders that stop the blood into the wound, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softens and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then use your index finger to see if any small sores remain, and cut and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the sore, you should not cut the sore at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall out through it without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire sore, you should bring together the two edges of the wound and stitch them now, since no excess has remained due to the size of the sore.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	You should then proceed to cut the root of it, and draw it out, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those sores that contain excess, pierce there where it appears ripe; and pierce it just as the previously mentioned one, in a dependent manner, then apply poultices with ointments and similar things, so that it destroys what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, treat it with a healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	Of quinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of throat surgery; but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with quinsy, it is necessary to drain the throat opening called the "epiglottis"; and one should not provide assistance by this method, because all the veins and the flesh of the sick are affected by those with abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the airway, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the death that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it under three or four small, transverse slits, between the two circles, or by the amount of the slit, not in the cartilage; and that place is so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are far from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the throat skin to the entire opening, then cut the skin until he reaches the airway; and drain the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the escape of phlegm from the airway through the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed of which one fears suffocation, bring together the two edges of the skin wound and suture it completely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the breathing fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then the epiglottis is cut because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days.  And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and cure it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a damsel take a knife and place it in her throat, and cut part of the airways of the windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and saw clearly that she had not cut any vein or conduit other than the throat, and the air was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and the damsel had no further affliction than a hoarse voice, and returned to her normal state.  Therefore, I say, that in the cutting of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and is a large abscess the color of a jaundice, and is most common in women; and it is according to two manners: natural and accidental; where the natural has no artifice.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one is similar to a fat swelling, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from a blood vessel; and there is fear, and it is not appropriate to work with fire except in the case of a small one, and to prove and search throughout the whole area; if you find it like a fat swelling, and it does not connect to any vein, then cut it, as one cuts swellings, and remove the entire mass, if there is any; and thoroughly search everything, and treat it as appropriate, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the swellings
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many types of swellings exist, of which I will describe all the appearances; and now it is necessary for me to describe all the differences between a swelling and a discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a discharge is accompanied by heat and fever, until the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a swelling, there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains a surface, which is its own sac, and is of the same color as the body, and begins like a blister and becomes large; and they are of two types, either greasy or moist, and many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treating the swelling, to first examine it with every instrument called “entromissoire”, according to its form as it will come in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses of swellings is that you should take the moistest area you find on the abscess and move your fingers gently, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, depending on the size of the abscess; then withdraw the instrument, and pay attention to what leaps out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If a running moisture flows, regardless of its color, lance it as I have said for other abscesses; and if no moisture comes after the instrument, know that it is greasy, then lance it in a cross shape, grasp it with tweezers, and gently scrape it from each side and watch the skin where it lies, making sure you remove it completely along with the swelling; and if you cannot remove it cleanly, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the swelling will return many times; and if a little remains, and the blood bothers you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and constrict the wound, and apply soothing hot poultices to the abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the swelling is large, stitch the two edges of the wound and treat it with remedies that promote the formation of scar tissue.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the throbbing vein is contrary to you or something else, hurry and fill the area with powdered vitriol, and leave it for two or three days, so that the wound rots and the boiling of the blood rests; then return to cauterizing what has remained of the swelling.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the probing instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are three types: large, medium, and small, for searching abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one stitches sores, and are made of yellow bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are better, and are more proven than black lead for searching the cavities of fistula; and they are of three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the probes are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are probes that have two curves of three types as well; and there are probes that have three curves, and are also of three types; and there are probes that have two curves, and probes with only one curve, and they are of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments that one uses is sharp, and some of them cut only on one side, with which one scrapes the sores, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and among these probes are the lancets mounted in handles, so that the patient does not feel it when opening abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, and sores, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to the peels of fruits, according to this shape, with which one stops the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the area that bleeds from the cutting of veins and arteries, and sometimes resembles this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must do so according to this shape from this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that generates flesh, then join the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the nipple droops and is softened because of its size, as happens with women, then cut it into two parts above, with two similar cuts; so that one is held to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened with corrosive ointment; and leave it until it devours the remaining part and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are like hard scrofulas where there are lumps, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofulas, then cut it as we have said in the cuts of scrofulas, and if the wound returns pus, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is stitched over it, there are often abscesses.  The same happens with swollen veins and abscesses; and if you know it is due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep. And when you feel it with your fingers, there is tightness. And if it is due to the vein, there are obvious swellings. It is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, in the ankles, in the neck, and in many other places, and is very large.
