Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to avoid iron treatment, and the one who is at the head must also be avoided, and in the one that is of swelling of the artery, cut through the skin with a long incision. Then open the incision with the lancets, and cleanly separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath it, and pierce it to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then pierce the area between the two threads with a probe until the blood that is there comes out, and the abscess is opened; then apply a treatment to drain the pus, until the thread falls out; then treat it with a suitable ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the vein cut, then you must hold with your hand the part of the abscess that is on all the skin, then place the needle under the area that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and place a double thread, so that you pull it through the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or the thread from one of the two sides to the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not stay, then place another needle along the entire thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the heart and leave what is tied; then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments with bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come to the artery and the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or through excessive exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often at the shoulders and in the fingers and in all places where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and is in various positions causing pain; and when it is squeezed strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but under the skin; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and those in the joints should not be cut with iron; perhaps contraction will result; and those on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, pierce it with a lancet and scrape it, then remove it and stitch the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes this occurs in the belly and nowhere else, a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to fungi.  The roots are subtle, the body large; and there are small and very large ones.  I saw a man who had two in his belly that resembled fungi more than anything else; there was no difference, they were white, had fine roots, were often split open, and moisture would often flow from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six.  The procedure for the incision is to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the growth is white and moist with subtle roots; cut it with a wide lancet, and have the fire cautery available.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting, there are often excessive bleedings of blood.  If the blood overwhelms you, then hasten to cauterize.  If you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, take a well-made lead thread and tie the growth as we have said, and leave it for two days.  Then restrain it and do not stop tightening the lead thread until it cuts the growth, and it breaks off cleanly without difficulty; and if the roots are large, fear to cut, especially in the belly, but you can cut it in half and then cauterize it so it does not return.  Then treat the wound and take care not to cut the growth, which is of a pale color and with poor understanding and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a festering abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is ripe.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the boil appears due to cautery of a wound or a surface fracture, and is on the belly, and some boils emerge, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries, as mentioned before, or from wind; and if it is due to the rupture of the surface and the emergence of the boil, the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and it opens through various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestines, then it is more diverse, and when you press it with your fingers, it pops up and then returns, and perhaps it is tight, and it grows considerably at the entrance of the bath and due to hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, and does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, the abscess appears large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or the vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, you must instruct the patient to hold their breath, and be stretched out straight, then make a sign around the wound; then tell them to lie still in your hands, then go around the place you have marked with all the spade, then extend half of the abscess above all the large one; then tie it around with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot be loose; then open half of the abscess extended over the knot, and put your index finger in it, and look for the intestine; if you find it caught in the knot, untie it, and put the intestine outside the belly; and if you find the bowel, grab it with a pin, and cut the excess; and if the artery or the vein opposes you, gently go around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you pierce; then squeeze the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you want, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and the dead flesh falls away on its own; or you cut it when it is thin and rotten, then treat it as necessary, and finish the abscess as we said; and remove the blood or moisture you find, then treat the place as necessary, and stitch the place.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the kinds of ulcers, and how one should work on them with medicine, and how to avoid iron treatment; and we say that the ulcer develops in the flesh, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be scraped, like ulcers on the breasts and thighs, and similar places, they should be completely removed when they are in the beginning; and when they are large and old, you should not approach them, for I have never cured one, nor has anyone ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make them bleed if there is evident fullness, then prepare the patient in a good place to do the work; then place your lancets on the ulcer, and cut around it on all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and press the place well with your hand or something, and if the flow of blood interferes with the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood stops; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed in the division the types of dropsy, how the accumulation of water occurs, the signs of each type, and the treatment using medicine and iron: only the 'eclytes' form is applicable.  One should not use iron in these two types: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy called 'eclytes' with medicine, and the treatment does not work, observe if the patient is weak, or if they have other illnesses besides dropsy, such as diarrhoea and similar things. Do not use iron in this case, because there is a risk.  And if you see a patient of strong constitution, and they have only dropsy as an illness, and they are not too young or too old, you should proceed as follows: lift the patient straight onto your hands, and apply pressure to the abdomen, pushing the water to the lowest part of the chest.  Then, using the spatumile espinous, in this manner...
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it have a point, but not so sharp that it could reach the intestines when inserted and cause injury; then, observe if the dropsy is located near the intestines: then you must cut above the belly, three fingers directly below the incision; and if the dropsy is caused by a liver ailment, make your incision on the left side of the belly, three fingers below; and if it is due to the spleen, it should be on the right; and it is not appropriate for the patient to lie on the incision so that the excess fluid does not flow to that weakened area; then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and remove it; and raise your hand with the spatumile between the skin and the surface, as if skinning it to the thickness of a fingernail or something similar; then pierce the surface until the spatumile reaches the hollow space, and this is the place where the water is; then drain it freely, and use this instrument which has this shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of bronze or light metal; and on the lower part, there is one small hole; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on another side, and one on the other; and the tip is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision, like a writer shapes a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is a small opening, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it will immediately descend onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than is necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die due to the resolution of his/her spirit, or he/she will fall unconscious, or approach death; but empty according to the strength of his/her constitution and according to what the patient's condition and pulse indicate; then remove the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained because the heart is stopping the hole that is above the surface, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the procedure the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and remove a small amount of water; do this repeatedly until only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient's condition, and you leave a lot of water, cure him with a hot grave or sand bath, and through profuse sweating, or a bath and the sun, and make him drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize the stomach, the liver, and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, immediately have it pierced with a very fine needle in this manner:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place a thin lead plug in the opening, bind it and keep it like this for three or four days. And when he wishes to urinate, remove the plug, let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it will not be necessary, for the urine that comes forth will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For those whose opening is small, the medicine of a lead plug, as we have said, will enlarge it.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are wounded, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the bladder, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient lies often on their back, then stretches the head of the penis and cuts it as if it were the cutting of a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should. And beware of the bleeding that often occurs; and if it happens, stop it with something that stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Abscesses on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils appear on the penis, and there is a hideous appearance of flesh; and some are malignant, and others not; you should take them with a fine probe, and cut and clean all of them, then apply moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, with a foul color and odor, you should apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the boil is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is within the skin and part outside, you must first remove the boil that is within; and when it is removed, treat the one outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, the shaft of the penis is not securely protected from being pierced, and blackness and corruption arise in the penis and scrotum; you must remove everything that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and quince, and treat it with further remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a discharge of blood occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this method:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two conditions together: namely, for blood discharge and corruption; and if the shaft of the penis is corrupt and retracted, you must insert a lead pipe into the penis, and the patient should urinate through it; and when the skin is inflamed at the head of the penis, which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or if it happens due to a wound or abscess, you must then cauterize it with a sharp instrument until the adhesions are broken, and the shaft of the penis is freed on all sides; and if this is a serious matter to separate, you should cauterize the head of the penis and the skin with a small spatula; then carefully separate the two, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, to prevent it from burning again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not simply the separation of a continuity like other wounds; however, when we undertake this operation willingly, and specifically on children, we must strive to perform the best and least painful operation possible for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, for they did not follow such a practice in their laws, and we only know about it from what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision with a knife, or forceps, or a scalpel;  the patient recoiled because there are two layers, and perhaps the upper layer is cut while the lower layer remains uncut.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or, it must be cut again, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing from the knife, the tip of the member is not always adequately cleaned; and when cleansing the skin with a knife, the blade perhaps slips, and the work is ruined, and many times wounds result that require further treatment, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing done with forceps, throughout the entire thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forceps cut evenly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts evenly at all times; but let the thread be tightly wrapped around the skin; and let the method of the first action be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and you can make him happy in every way that you can; then hold it between your hands straight, and place the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow into the wound, and pull it up until the head of the penis is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below one stitch to another stitch; and hold it with your two fingers by the second stitch to the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two stitches, then quickly lift the wound and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood flow slowly, for this is the remedy; and put powder on top, and over the powder a thin layer of glue made from a boiled egg diluted with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forceps for cleansing is this: the two heads should be sharp and the heads should be as large as the handles, equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the cleansing is when the wound is inside the incision; then it is necessary that you spread it with your fingernail, so that the place does not become an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it passes three days, and that which is under the penis is swollen, leave it until the inflamed abscess has subsided, and lightly scrape it; cut it as you can, and be careful to avoid the part of the penis, this will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with the remedies for wounds, as we have said in treating powders, and if the wound is cut beyond measure, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to an obstruction by a stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention is due to a stone lodged in the neck of the bladder, the patient must be bent over his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and he should extend his stomach from the upper part of his back, and the patient should strain as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is forced to express the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer an extraction using a tool called a "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine, light silver, like the feather of a bird; and it should be a palm and a half long, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for releasing the urine is to take a double thread, and tie a small piece of wool or cotton to the end, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and push it to the tip of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a seat, and lubricate the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then pull the penis upwards towards the groin; then push the syringe forward towards the bladder, and the patient will feel it reaching the empty area, and this is not always done in this order, because sometimes the channel it goes through is twisted; then pull the thread with the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and make the urine flow; and repeat the use of the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient should be relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction gathers there, and you wish to distill liquids and medicines into it, use the instrument called a "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the narrow passage through which the medicine flows should be such that it tightly seals the penis without additional material, so that one can draw out the moisture and insert when necessary; and when you wish to inject your medicines into the bladder, put the tip of the instrument into the moisture, and pull the part within; then you will draw the moisture into the instrument, and then push the part within forcefully; then the moisture will enter, and immediately reach the bladder, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the slender clyster with which one clysters the bladder: thus it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or bronze, and has a wider end; and below is a narrow part where the ligature falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture with which you wish to clyster the bladder into it, then tie it between the two narrow parts using a strong doubled thread, and heat a little of that moisture over the fire; then insert the tip of the clyster into the penis, and press with your hand on the bladder until all the moisture flows in, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle from it, and pierce it evenly around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a seal, and put inside what you wish for oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the types of stones, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have discussed the difference between stones formed in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what stones one should perform surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will explain it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones formed in the bladder occur more often in children, and it is a sign that water escapes from the bladder, similar to water in its thinness; and it shows grit, and the patient scratches their penis, and it hangs down many times, and then stiffens; and many of these escapes damage the foundation; and the cure is easier in children until they are four years old, and is very difficult in old men, and is average in those between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, to remove all the waste from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes emerges from the upper part; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downward; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten to cut into the stone immediately.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out entirely when touched, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young adult; and place it on his foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, pull it towards the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it outwards where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand towards the nipples upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin beneath the nipples in the area where the incision is made; then place the scalpel there, which has this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between that which is between the nipples and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left groin; and it should be straight above the stone, and your fingers should always be on the foundation, and the incision should be wider outwards and narrower inwards, according to the size of the stone, not too wide; perhaps the pressure from the finger on the foundation will make it jump out without difficulty; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: this makes them hard to remove; and there are some that are smooth, like a pebble, and round, from which removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must tighten with pliers which are like a file at the head, to grip the stone so that it does not escape; or you should place a thin curved instrument underneath; and if you cannot extract it thus, slightly enlarge the opening, and if the blood flows, then staunch it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, remove the largest one first to the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then push it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be softened, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out repeatedly through the opening because the area cannot close; but nevertheless, try to pull it out, or break it with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a moistened cloth in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then wrap the patient around his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, thoroughly wash the area with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon and basilicon ointments until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses, ulcers, and blood clots occur in the bladder, and urine is retained in this manner, with blood coming out with the urine, then insert your finger into the wound and remove the blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder; then cleanse the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help him in every way you can until he is healed; and you must bind his legs together every time you treat him, and assemble the medicines on the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot exit, treat it as I have said before, by cutting it many times.  The cutting is excused by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron implement in this shape, with three angled points joined in a fork.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so it cannot return to the bladder; then gently insert the implement into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the implement in your hand against the stone bit by bit until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will soon come out, and then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is then broken, and it jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the urethra at the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the threads, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will reveal herself to onlookers, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a knowledgeable woman in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone in a woman is deeper than a man's stone, so more profound cutting is needed, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity commands this, then you must take a skilled midwife, and one is rarely found, and if you find none, then seek a discreet, chaste onlooker; and present a wise and experienced woman in the life of women, or a woman knowledgeable in part of the art, and instruct her to do what you instruct her to do regarding the inquiry into the stone; and watch carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must put her finger on the fundament and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then she must hold it under her finger, and instruct her to put her finger in where the disease is and to press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut at the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the vulva, where the stone is apparently located, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her finger over or under the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then place a rod in the incision, if you feel the stone, widen the wound until the stone can be pulled out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	So know the appearances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overwhelms you, apply powdered vitriol, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stanched; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments I have told you about for the extraction of stones in men to assist you in your work; and if the blood overwhelms you, and it is from the artery that has been cut, then place the powder on the area, and bandage tightly with cloth strips and bandages, and do not start this again, and leave the stone and do not extract it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the area is healed, then return to your work, until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white fluid, beneath the skin of the testicles, which holds the egg; and it is called "white fluid," and sometimes it is properly in the tissue of the egg, so that one might think it another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white fluid we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colours: either it is a colour leaning towards jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs for recognizing this collection, for if it is the white fluid that we have mentioned, it is a soft abscess, a little long, like the shape of an egg, and the testicle does not appear, for there is moisture all around it.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the actual tissue, it is a soft abscess with a part of the egg, and because of that one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white fluid, one feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the colour of the moisture, test along the whole inside, in the shape that has been shown before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, that which comes after the internal examination, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be bled according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then place him on his back, on a slightly raised surface, and put many cloths underneath him; then sit him on his left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the testicles; then take the leached sponge, and cut the skin of the testicles along its length, right up to the point of the knife, and let your incision be perfectly straight, dividing the skin of the testicles down to the white fluid, and carefully scrape it according to your ability; then pierce the white fluid with a wide opening and drain all the fluid, then apply your hooks, and spread the white fluid upwards; and do not touch the core of the testicles, but only the white fluid; cut completely or in pieces, very carefully, the sides of it, for if you do not cut it wisely, the fluid will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, return it to its place once you have completed the work on the white fluid; then stitch the two edges of the skin of the testicles together, then treat it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another disease, you must tie the vessels that are supporting it, in fear of the leakage of blood; then cut the testicle completely from its support, remove the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if fluid has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; cut the other part as you did the first one, likewise, then wipe away the blood, and place moist wool in rose oil in the wound; and place another wool moistened in wine and oil, and put it over the two testicles, and place doubled cloths on top, and tie it tightly, in the manner described in this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with charpie wool according to this shape, and sew them together at the groin of the breeches, and one of the ends should be placed on the fundament down to the back, and the other at the area of the knife; and the other end over the two groins, and the entire bandage should be gathered in the buckle of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of iron cutting, and that you take a thin, knife-like cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we said, so that the white fluid that contains the liquid is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that fluid with the hooks, and scrape it with this hot, thin cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in every way you can, until you remove everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the testicle; and know that this work is safer; and observe the precautions against leakage of blood, and do not perform this work unless you are careful; and if anything opposes you, or abscess, or leakage of blood, or anything else, then treat what opposes you, according to what has been previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its fearsome nature, perform a puncture, as I tell you, and this means that when you are certain, through the signs we have described, that the watery branch is present, have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess on the lower side of the entire spine, and make the puncture in line with the body; and the opening should be large enough for all the fluid to drain; then put cotton on the area and tie it, and let the remaining fluid drain, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit through the opening of the wound, you must insert a tube or the instrument used to remove fluid from those with dropsy, whose shape is described earlier; and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the fluid returns and gathers again after six months or less, and when it gathers again as before, thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this condition there are many fears and various dispositions, therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the procedure and the characteristics of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses occur in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say, through an excess of acrid and sharp humor, which spreads to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not cause much pain, and is a serious abscess; and perhaps some serious abscesses are frightening and hard, and of dark color, and sometimes come from a rupture of an artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to a rupture of an artery, it is recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	The one caused by vein swelling is recognized by its disposition to the touch of your fingers, and one can properly make an incision on this kind, and on other parts; and that you cut the skin of the testicles, then pull the testicle upwards, and draw the white membrane downwards, and free the suspensory ligament from all sides of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the testicle is already embedded with these surrounding tissues, then you must pull the testicle, and cut it; and if it is airy on the surface, or within the vessels, you must then release all of that membrane, and cut it neatly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the tissue is in the rear, you must cut it all, and remove the testicle, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enclosed by a swelling similar to a boil, accompanied by softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when moving; and the treatment for this illness is just as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and nonetheless, we will tell you the method, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspensory of the testicles down to your fingers, holding all the vessels near the penis, and let the masters grasp them and stretch them firmly; then cut with a sharp, wide scalpel through the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape on each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the viscera have emerged, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with other boils, making sure no vessels supplying one of the testicles are severed; because if this is done, it causes no harm, and if pus comes from all vessels, the testicles must be severed from all vessels, so the organ does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and becomes dry and unable to recover.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the scrotum.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	This condition arises from a tear in the scrotum, or from stretching in the groin area, causing the intestines to descend into one of the testicles; and this rupture is either of the scrotum itself or from stretching it.  These two types of causes come from many things: blows, falls, straining, or lifting heavy loads, and similar actions.  The signs when it's from stretching the scrotum are that it happens gradually, over a long time, and does not occur suddenly; and the abscesses are uniform down to the depths, because the scrotum presses against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it's a tear in the scrotum are that it causes sudden pain at the onset, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin, close to the surface, because of the intestines protruding and pushing through the scrotum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the testicles descend with the intestines, and become trapped, causing the patient great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of fear, regarding iron, one should avoid it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method is that you instruct the patient to push the intestines back into the wound with your hand if possible; then, hold it on their neck, between your hands, and lift their thighs.  Then, stretch the scrotum upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert forceps according to need to open the wound and ensure the testicles can exit.
