Then, cut away the scrotum beneath the skin of the testicles, exposing the tough white scrotum completely; then, push your index finger into what’s behind the testicle, between the white scrotum beneath the skin and the second layer, and separate what's behind the testicle, and between the second layers. Then, move your right hand inside the scrotum, and stretch the white tough scrotum upwards with your left hand, and lift the testicle with all of the scrotum towards the groin; instruct the assistant to pull the testicle upwards, and to loosen what’s above the binding. Check with your fingers if any intestine is wrapped in the tough white scrotum, and if you find anything, push it back into the abdomen.  Then, take a needle with a thick thread made of 10 strands, and place it in the back of the scrotum, behind the skin of the testicles; after the incision, cut the ends of the thread until there are four strands.  Then, tie them together in a cross pattern and bind the scrotum, which we spoke of as being beneath the skin of the testicles, with a strong bandage on both sides;  wrap the ends of the thread, and tie them tightly on both sides, so that none of the vessels that feed them can enter, so that no inflammatory abscesses form.  Then, lay the bandage again with the first bandage overlapping by two fingers, and after these two bandages, leave an inch of scrotum beneath the scrotum and the rest according to the shape of the testicle.  Then, cut in the area beneath the skin of the testicles, until the blood flows, and the wound heals, as we stated before; then apply wool soaked in oil to the wounds, and apply the bandage we described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white scrotum, as we have described, is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the bandage remain until it falls off on its own; and if it takes a long time to fall off, it should be soaked with warm water, and apply what we have said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with other remedies until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch that binds the viscera, in this manner: tie the vessels, after cutting slightly above or below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of what opens, until the vessels fall out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs within the intestines, as we have said, and the area opens; and none of the intestines descend into the groin, and if any do descend, it is little, and repairs itself every hour; and yet, if it remains too long in this state, the wound or opening grows, until the intestines descend; and this happens due to the stretching of the opening in the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then the area softens and swells and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: the patient lies on their back between your hands; then cut the area of the ruptured, swollen opening as wide as three fingers; and then remove the tissue beneath the skin that covers it; then take the reed and place it over the visible area of the tissue; and press it into the depth of the abdomen, then stitch the two visible areas of the tissue above the head of the reed, and stitch both together; then remove the head of the reed, and do not cut into the tissue or stretch the sac or anything else, as I have shown you in the treatment of intestinal hernias; then treat it using the method for treating wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sac is constricted, and does not appear at the rupture, and cauteries are milder in this location, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the groin
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the groin softens in some men, because the tissues within are softened, and it is noticeable; and when one wishes to cure it, it is necessary to have the patient lie on their back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then bring the two edges together with a stitch, and if you wish, first stitch the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
dou chastrement	of the castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is condemned in our law, and for that reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is that the students must be able to answer when asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the way we do by pulling, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the testicles are softened and hanging; then grasp them with your hand, until they are drawn back and you feel them no longer.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For castration by incision: you must restrain the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut each testicle in one stroke, once you have well skinned them; and leave a little of the surface and the delicate surface that is over the vessels; and this way of castration is milder than the one done by pulling, because in pulling perhaps some part of the testicles remains, by which the beast desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways in men: one is that between the two testicles appears a figure like that of a woman, or there is hair, and sometimes urine flows there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and they have a penis like a male and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for the man and the woman is that you cut all the joined flesh, and treat it like other wounds; in the second case, of men whose urine escapes through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tentigene
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a joined flesh on the natural part, when it is too ugly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must remove the excess flesh of the tentigene with your hand or tweezers, and cut it slightly; and do not go too deep, lest there be a flow of blood, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; and there is another flesh that grows at the mouth of the wound, and fills it, and perhaps bursts open, and resembles a cow, and therefore the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it, as we have said of the tentigene, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of the erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the woman's natural passage is not open, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental through illness that has come upon her; or it is due to joined flesh, or a thin or thick membrane, and is formed deep within the wound, or in the sides, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps the ability to bear children; and the knowledge of this is through examination of the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the blockage is readily apparent, try with your fingers or a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a thin membrane, and it is close to the two lips, hurry, and do it like this: place your two index fingers together, and the woman lie on her back, legs spread; then spread the two lips gently, until the thin membrane is loosened, and the blockage is open; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman lie on her back every day, so it cannot close up.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the membrane is hard and thick, you must cut it with a scalpel, resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the blockage is of formed flesh, remove it with a forceps and cut it; and have medicines that stop bleeding, as needed, like dragon's blood, frankincense, and egg white mixed together; then apply a wide lead strip, so that the wound cannot close; and let it stay for a long time, and apply a dry linen tent; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when formed flesh appears in the wound, it must be cut according to this method, unless it is an encrusted abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an encrusted abscess in the wound, one should not use fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become inflamed; and we have already discussed their types and signs, and I will now describe those that receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and inflammation, when deep within the wound and not apparent to the touch, are not cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the wound, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must put the woman in a cold house, then seize the inflammation with forceps, and cut it at its roots, then apply powders of blood-stopping medicines, such as oak galls, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, gallnuts, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without causing wounds; then take wool and soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh boil, so it must be cut as I said for the inflammation; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the breast.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the breast, such as ulcers, stony abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and several other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is fitting, then, that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the breast, which is not one of the abscesses that collect pus; and if you wish to know the treatment for it, observe if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not rush to pierce it, but allow it to mature until the pain subsides; and then have the sick person sit on a seat, and let them have two small seats where they can lean, and rest on their back and bring their feet towards the outside of the leg; and let their thighs be spread, and let them put their arms under their knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then, gently draw the patient's chest towards the right side, and apply the instrument used to open the breast cavity, the design of which will be shown later.  And when you wish to apply this instrument, you must first insert a probe to determine the depth of the breast, so that whatever enters the instrument does not go deeper than necessary and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, the depth of the breast must be covered with cloths so that the instrument does not cause harm; and they should place the cone of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and it is gently incised by hand, it must be cut off at the top, to the level of the incision; and when the pus is emptied, you must place moist cloths soaked in rose oil, or dry green oil, into the wound.  Place the cloth deep inside the wound, towards the breast cavity, and place over the wound and the incision clean wool soaked in water, or boiled mallow root; then treat it with the appropriate ointments for two days, until it is healed.  And sometimes, the breast and wound are cleaned with a clyster of water and honey, then with water or boiled roots of lilies and aristolochia; and then return to the ointments.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is reopened in the breast, you must avoid using iron cauterization, but treat it as we have described in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	First, the midwife must understand the natural pattern of childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press downwards and desire to smell the air. Then the child hastens to emerge.  Know then that this childbirth is according to nature, and the child exits under its head, and the placenta with it; and when you see these signs, it is appropriate to gently press her abdomen so that the child emerges quickly; because when it descends beneath its head, the placenta emerges with it, and the breast cavity is cleaned of its superfluities by good cleansing.  And that which emerges differently is not natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes emerges on its feet, and the body or head, and hands emerge, or it emerges on its stomach, or back, and is perhaps twisted around its neck, and by other bad positions.  Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and to guard against error and deception. And I will show you all the positions, how one should aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child emerges under its head through a natural delivery, and the woman is labouring hard, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and apply a mixture of oil or fenugreek to the area, and then the midwife should put between her fingers the small spatumile, whose shape is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the placenta, and cut with her fingernail until the moisture within is released; and grasp the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to enema the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then make her drink and induce her to sneeze with a concoction and hold her mouth and nose for an hour; then the child will emerge now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands emerge, it is necessary to gently bring them back one by one; and if they cannot re-enter, place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet; then lower the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so she doesn't fall when it is lowered. And if the hands cannot re-enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife previously mentioned, and take out the child, and bring them back likewise.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's emergence on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it must be pushed upwards; and then it is turned slowly until it is aligned; then take one of the feet and extend it slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it leaps down to the thighs, instruct her to grasp it, and make her sneeze with a concoction; if it leaps out, if God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, turn it slowly until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a mixture of alum, and oil of rosemary, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and apply this ointment to the woman's nature, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened underneath, apply a compress of myrrh, and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, make her sneeze, and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will now leap out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's delivery on her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the midwife should gently place her hands on it; then hold it over her neck, and hang the feet downward, and let it lie on a bed; and gently bend her hands, and then place her hands on her belly, and remove the cushions from underneath, until she is ready to deliver; and if the child does not leap out, take its feet and move them forcefully, then move the belly upwards, then push with your hands; and pull the child slowly; and instruct the woman to bear down until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes out with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand; if it cannot be brought back, make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie on a bed, and straighten her legs forcefully; then administer the ointment I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; and pull the child according to its natural form, make her sneeze, and tell her to push until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child on the mother's back, with its arms outstretched, and its face turned towards the mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the midwife to hold its hand, then turn it gently, and pull it gently; and when it is aligned, put the healing ointment and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move gently; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and tell her to push; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way for the entire afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way for the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth at the fingernail level so that the moisture is emptied; and if the child hangs by its face and its neck, cut it from the opening so that it is not retained and the child dies; then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and tell the woman to push sometimes; then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the delivery of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens little.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if little; I know that, they are multiplied, and are separated by the surface that divides them, which is attached to the opening; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one whole, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and quickly and easily do what she must; and do so as it suits them for safety.
de plusors enfans	Of several children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or several up to fifteen, and are entirely formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the wise and glorious, and it is necessary that the midwife know all this, for perhaps such a thing happens to her; so do as is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman of a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; the woman must be placed on her back, and her head tilted down, and her legs raised; and the minister should hold her from two sides, or she be tied to the bed so that she is not pulled down by the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of elecampane, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then the midwife should anoint her hands with these oils and mixtures; then gently put them in the womb, then find a place where she puts the hooks that are suitable for this, and be watchful if the child is prepared to descend on its head; place the hooks in its eyes or its neck or mouth or its palate or under the chin or in the armpit or near the sides, and if the descent is on its feet, place the hook in its heels or in the middle ribs; and it is necessary that she hold the hook in her right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of her left hand, and gently put it in her whole hand, and place the hook in any of these places that we have said, until it reaches the empty place; and this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place another hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then extend it equally by moving it from side to side, to cause it to come out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold it, as this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if part of it remains, the midwife should anoint some of her fingers with oil, and put them in that part, and pull the other part; and if anything remains, place the hook in a higher place, and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to constriction, you must wrap it in a cloth until it all comes out; then cut it at the joint of the sole or with a knife, and likewise you must do with the other hand, and with the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and the passage is narrow, or it has a sharp point gathered on the head, you must place the pointed spatula between your fingers, and cut the head and remove the point; or you may remove it with the instrument called "almidach," whose shape is shown with the instruments in the following chapter; and likewise do the same if the child has a naturally large head; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and is stuck in the armpit, let it be cut until the moisture that is in the bottom comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the extraction is gentle, and the repositioning at the mother's mouth is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is constricted in the belly or chest, you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and cut the belly or chest until the moisture within flows out; and if other limbs are removed, and the head remains, the midwife puts her hand deep inside the mother's, and pulls it down to the mother's mouth; then places a hook or two and pulls it out; and if the mother's mouth is contracted due to a hot abscess that has arisen, do not work on it, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and apply plasters, and soak in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, apply what we have said about a live child; and if one cannot, pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about hot abscesses that come in the mother; and if bleeding occurs, immerse it in constricting water, and apply other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had contained a dead child, then another was sewn on top of it, and the second died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared in the buttock, and swelled until it opened, and began to greatly discharge pus.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and pondered it for a long time, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong-drawing plaster, and a bone came out, and after a few days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I greatly marvelled at this, for there are no bones in the belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it must be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived a long time like this, and a little pus would often come from the place; and I have only recorded this chapter because, when masters encounter a strange thing, they should know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to restore the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here after comes the form of the press, with which the books were made; and with two turns at the two ends of the two hinges.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the cylinder should be one finger wide, and the margin of the timbers one finger, and a palm and a half long; and between the two hinges should be two joints of this same cylinder, which should be fastened on one and on the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and have two joints at the two ends, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the marrow with the whole instrument, have the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging and legs open, then place the two assembled joints into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then operate your hand on the entire instrument, as you did with the pliers similarly, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the marrow, until the marrow does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all topped, and their forms are multiplied; and when the master has prepared them, the work is all the faster, and more elevated for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect the instrument until you have prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with condiments, and grasp her mouth and nose with your hands; and if she expels it by doing so, well and good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over the fire; then put one end of a cane into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the marrow, and hold it until the vapors come into the marrow; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The afterbirth will be expelled quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out easily, instruct the woman to wet her left hand in linseed oil or in marshmallow tea, and then apply it to the area, and search for the afterbirth; and when she has found it, she should grasp it gently and pull it straight, so that the marrow does not burst during the extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled; it will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the marrow is tightly constricted, we have described the treatment of sneezing and herbal fumigation; and if it does not come out from all that we have said, take care not to pull too hard; but you should tie what is at the opening of the marrow to the woman's thigh, then give her a clyster of tetrapharmacon ointment; this will soften it and restore it, and it will come out easily; however, when it softens, a bad odor arises in the stomach and head, and injures the woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are needed for this: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman in the retention of the flowers and afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a chain, and one places the fine end in the area, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be over the embers, and the cloth burn until it is consumed, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but it is blocked by a thin film; therefore, the midwife must pierce this film with her finger, and do not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and take care that she does not injure the surrounding tissue; then she should apply wool soaked in wine and oil, and then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will close up again, place a lead chain in the opening and leave it there for several days, and it should be removed when the child can be taken to the chamber pot.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these blockages come from the closure of a wound or an abscess; therefore, one must cut through this closure, and treat it as we have described with the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from beneath the fundament are swellings, and those that come from beside the fundament or in the space between the two parts, have a fistula or several; and when this swelling is old, it opens and discharges white or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are piercing; and they are recognized by the fact that either dung or gas comes out when the patient defecates, and perhaps a worm jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce down to the bladder and even to the middle of the penis; and they reach down to the joint of the thigh and even to the navel.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a fistula that pierces the fundament, and not one that does not; and that you put your index finger on the fundament, and put a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is a twisting, you put a thin lead tent, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there comes no dung, gas, or worm from the opening, as we have said, know that it does not pierce; hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces to the bladder or the passage of urine, urine leaks from it and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces to the joint of the thigh, the tent goes down to the place; if there is no twisting, and the source of the pain is around it, it often discharges pus, and no medicine or ointment can heal or close it; and in these piercing fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the folly of meddling charlatans.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not piercing and not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced.  The patient lies on their back in your hands; you lift their legs up to their thighs, and bend their thighs towards their belly.  Then put a bronze tent, or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the bottom, you should put your index finger there; then if you feel the tent has pierced it, and it is open where you feel the surface or flesh between your finger, then know that it has pierced; do not work on it if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	However, it is said that some can be healed, but this is rare; and the help given is that the fine cautery is heated according to the width of the fistula, as previously mentioned; and it is put hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the bottom; and do this two or three times, until you know that these furrowed flesh are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then treat it with softened tents in butter, until that flesh comes out; then treat with ointment that causes flesh to grow and heal.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters, but does not pierce to the finger that is at the bottom, and there is a thick layer of flesh or surface between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula at the edge of the covering of the wound; then cut it from the beginning of the fistula, and again insert the tent, and then apply the cautery until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be released, and fall out; then clean the charred flesh, which looks like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overwhelms you, and flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For cauteries of fire combine two good things: that is to say, the burning of these added flesh, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat with softened tents in butter or ground herbs, until the wound discharges pus, and the burned flesh comes out in the pus; then treat the wound with healing ointments that grow strong flesh, and the remedies are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula reaches the bottom of the foundation, and is distant from the body, place your finger at the bottom and investigate that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between the two is the cloth or the surface or flesh, where it is about to break through, there are no other means than faith and hope, through administering one of these three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, you put in tents and treat it as first; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the structure that holds the foundation, and the expulsion comes from a way not of your choosing; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it since it is cut next to the foundation, either with a tent or with another suitable instrument; then cleanse the damaged flesh that is in the wound as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound and keep the fistula on the outside part of the foundation; this will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are in this way: and it is when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation next to the skin above, take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one twisted thread into two, and place the tent with all the thread in the fistula until it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing the edge of the foundation inside, then pull the thread from that hole, just as you place your finger on the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and leave it for one or two days; and hold it sometimes, until the thread cuts the flesh that is between the two, and they fall; then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make the incision so deep for the lacing, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatulim, with which one opens the fistula, is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two types: either they are inside the fundament, like resin grains, and there are small and large ones, and often blood flows from them, and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the body; and the treatment for those that are inside the fundament is that you instruct the patient to strain himself to go to the latrine, so that the fundament protrudes and the filaments appear; then quickly, and pull them with pliers, or hold them with your fingernail, then cut them at their roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder them with some hot powders that are in place of cauterization; or if you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then you enema the patient with a biting and harsh enema to wash what is in the fundament, so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains and the filaments are outside the fundament, the treatment is easy; and that you take them with your fingernail or with pliers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must administer the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and it should be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do likewise for all the others, and leave one to run the excess of blood; then put a cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerote on the fundament, and put it on the fundament, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they fall, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointments and other treatments until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the pus in the fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is a drying of pus in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape the crust off with a spatula or your fingernail, so that it doesn't get moist; then treat it until it is healed as appropriate; and if it cannot heal, then re-scrape it more forcefully than before, until it bleeds a lot and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small, deceptive appearance around the body, and goes very deep; and sometimes the cold is found there, and one feels it as if trembling, and it spreads throughout the body, and more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is to take a twig of goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that twig on the tremor, so that the circle surrounds the tremor entirely; then turn your hand along the whole twig until you cut around the tremor, and dig it deep, and remove the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one of copper or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and pointed above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not pierced, in order to hold it to the finger, and to press it. And if you wish, cauterize the tremor, as it is previously described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or gold, or of melted or wrought copper; and sometimes these instruments are made small or large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which are administered to children and to those who are weak and sorrowful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is thus wider at the top, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a separation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the bottom should be pierced; and there should be two holes on one side, and one on the other; and the belly, where one places the medicines, should be of an animal's bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one inch of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread of spun thread twisted in an X or around, and assemble the belly like a purse; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the clyster; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently insert it; then the administrator presses it with both hands together, until it is completely full, then withdraws the clyster, and the patient raises their legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps soundly all night, that is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer it in a disease of belly discharge, and the medicine is quick to exit, repeat it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, the clyster should be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin clyster, where the leather is constricted:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed the division of the treatment of wounds; now we will discuss the treatments of hands and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by throwing stones, and cuts from swords and knives, or spears or wood or arrows, or similar things; or where they are made according to the parts of the body, like a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from a thrown stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless broken and the wound is large, and you fear a hot abscess might develop: then make it bleed immediately from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be towards the opposite side of the injured part; and keep the patient from consuming much wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not wish to bleed, let its food be reduced, and let it drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, if the wound is fresh with all its blood, and it is not discolored by the air, put powder on it, which I will say a little later; and if the burn has discolored it, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by bandages, bring them together by stitching, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the ribs.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone, and hanging, and held only by a little bit, cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as roasted meats and cooked grains, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, cut all the rot out and burn it, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, seek out the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help at all, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light; and it is that you put this powder on, which will reunite it even if the burn has discolored it.
