Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coals three parts, and powder it finely, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coals alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the burn has not discolored the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has discolored the wound, especially in its state, one does not put this powder on it; but puts on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made from water and honey, until it is well-soaked; then treats it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then hold it with fine pincers; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment, and to not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is also with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as warm wash in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and warm wash also in soft water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is festered and full of pus, pierce it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, then separate it, and tie it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is protected, through which the food goes, stitch the heart onto the throat's tissue, and do not touch the throat but place it back according to its natural shape; and then restrain the swelling and leave it for several days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has caused an impression in the bone, seek it out; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all that you can, and those that you cannot remove, let them remain until the wound becomes rotten, and the outflow is separated and lightened; and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, observe if wind escapes from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply the powder in the first hour, nor bind it because of the blood lest it remains deep and returns to the heart, and kills the patient; but put an attracting ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, place old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound for three, or four, or more days; thus no spasms or bad tremors or constrictions of breathing will occur; and when you see the good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then cure it with tents and other treatments until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and opens up again, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, on the chest or the back, treat it as previously mentioned; if it is large, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is deep into the bone, and has broken pieces, search the wound, and remove them if they are detached; and if they are not detached, allow the wound to fester, as removal will lighten the burden; and the judgment on other wounds of other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large, medium, and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, jump out, causing their entanglement; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because more effort is required to return the intestines, if they are not returned immediately; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, and thus return with more difficulty, and therefore a medium wound is better, because the intestines are more easily returned to their place than in the other two. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four kinds: two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body, and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more specific with the suture of the belly, and I will describe each and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, and it is difficult to return, this is through one of the two ways: either due to the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine has swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a linen cloth in slightly warm water, or cook it in water with vinegar and cypress and spices, and apply it to the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes this astringent wine is better than plain water for deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or cooked elder and mallows, because this makes entry easier with little effort; and if it cannot enter, slightly open the wound with an instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than cutting, which should not be done without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: it cuts inwards in a curve and not outwards, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine jumps out, return it gently to its natural place, if you can, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the stomach, then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and if the rupture of the stomach is in one of the two parts, pay attention that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to apply what I say to large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply the appropriate remedies, then have a skilled assistant hold the entire rupture in their hand and bring the edges together; and this is the common method of stitching: take one or more needles, according to the size of the wound, leave an inch of space from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread; pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the underlying skin (the subcutis) until you have pierced through on that side, and bring the four edges together; then tie a double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring together the two edges of the wound and leave an inch of space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue this until the whole wound is stitched; the needles should be of medium size, between fine and thick, as fine needles cut all the flesh, and overly thick ones cannot enter properly; therefore, they must be of medium size; and do not push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and disrupt the wound before it heals; then cut the ends of the needles so they do not injure the patient while they sleep, and place pads or bandages over the needle tips to keep them in place, and leave them there until the wound heals; this method of needle stitching is more suitable for small wounds, as one or two needles are sufficient.  The second method of stitching is common, and it involves bringing together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the underlying skin with a needle and strong medium thread; and when you have pierced all four edges together, return the needle to the starting point, like sewing cloth; and leave the space between each stitch the width of a little finger; this method of stitching is known by men, and I stitched a wound a man had in his abdomen, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was over an inch wide, and the intestines protruded over two inches, and the wound was in the middle of the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was stitched up in 15 days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and that was a miracle; and I did not treat it with ointments, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I just put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and push it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the skin straight through, leave the edge of the subcutaneous tissue where you have inserted the needle, and pierce it from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch like a tanner does leather, and that you leave the subcutaneous tissue on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen properly describes, is like some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and place one edge of the subcutaneous tissue against the other, in this way: insert a needle into the nearby edge of the skin, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two edges of the subcutaneous tissue; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside to the inside, through the two edges of the subcutaneous tissue; then pierce each of them from outside to inside, in two other skin edges on the other side; and this is the simplest and most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this, and some testify, that one should stitch the abdomen with two needles, with thread on each; and one should insert one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who stitch leather; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, the stitching is more severe than in other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the wound is like the treatment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, before the pus has changed it, put the intestines back in place and stitch it; then apply powder of healing paste, and if the pus has changed it, apply any available ointment until the wound begins to heal; and the threads are pulled out, the skin and the skin are sutured; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to discharge pus, apply old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will spread to the principal limbs, you should soak light wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the ankles and under the armpits; and if pain or rotting in blisters is felt, and this happens often, apply warm black wine enemas, especially if the rot reaches the intestines; and pierce it internally, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when wounded, and this is because of the abundance of veins in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the ligament (zirbe) protrudes from the wound, put it back in place just like the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned dark or black, you must bind the black area so that no bleeding occurs, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the tie, and hang the two ends down from the part under the wound downwards, to facilitate extraction when the ligament falls out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I saw a man who was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became festered and turned into a fistula, and there came out excretions and gases; I applied treatment according to what I could, and I did not cease to treat until it was healed, and the wound closed up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it heal, I feared that the patient might have pain in his belly; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in this way: take a leech with large heads, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the leech has opened its mouth, place it on the two edges, so that it closes its mouth around them; and then cut off its head, and it will remain in place so that it cannot detach itself; then put another leech on it in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These leeches adhere to the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestines with a fine thread which is cut from the intestines of an animal, in this way: take the end of this intestinal thread, which is very lean, and then tie a thread of fine twisted linen to the end of this thread; then put the thread into a needle and stitch the intestines, and bring them together at the rupture; and this method of leech stitching is nothing more than a matter of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the large intestines, there is no device or skill, but only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes festered, is universally called "fistula," especially when it is festered and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula, in truth, is a hardened and white knotted swelling, where no pain is felt, and is as festered as the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it discharges clear pus, and sometimes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes quite a lot; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is only because of one of the eight causes: namely, by the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the edges, which prevents flesh from growing; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the digestion is slow in the region, and healing is slow, and it swells by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to tell you the cure for a fistula that is made by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the surface, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and some come to the property of the main limb, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident of its cure, and want to know it, take a copper or iron probe, if the fistula is straight, search with it; and if the fistula is crooked, search with a thin lead probe, for lead bends easily around the curves; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot properly search it with probes, irrigate it through one of the openings, as the moisture will flow from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then search it carefully to your ability, so you can know if there are bones or nerves, and if it is festering deeply, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and the place where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, cut it according to what I have said, and remove completely the hardened and corrupted flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in the right place, you must cut deep as much as you can, then put moistened probes in sharp medicine and place them at the top of the fistula, so that the medicine eats away the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments to regenerate healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the main limb, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, cleanse it until all the corruption is removed, then cure it with things that regenerate flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and pus returns as before, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can remove with pliers, remove it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, remove them all, leaving none; and if the moisture resists, and there is no error or fear, cut the moisture and flesh, and expose the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, apply something to the wound to cause the flesh around the bones to rot, and then the bones will be more easily extracted; and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, cleanse the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large portion of the corruption, reaching the marrow of the bone, it must be cleaned and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cured until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that originated inside his body, until the matter reached his leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to avoid opening it; but the doctors, in their folly, worked on it so much that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared that all emitted pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors treated it for about two years, and there was no skilled person in the art of medicine until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed from the openings in great quantity; and the young man's body was becoming red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hastened, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached the bone within; I cleaned what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, except that which I removed; and began to restore the wound with healing remedies for a long time, but it could not heal; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued into the bone, and I cleaned it and then removed it, and I tried to heal the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm's breadth of the bone, and removed it completely to its marrow, then I restored it with medicines; and he was healed and healed quickly, and it was not necessary to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation, he often coughed, but he was completely healed, and a hard flesh grew in the place of the bone, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or hindrance at all, neither in his air nor in his going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take a bandage, and bind it to the head of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to extend it upward; and place another bandage of wool thicker than the first bandage, and bind it over the flesh that is above the bone, and extend the head, so that you pull the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh over the place where you want to treat, so that the treatment does not injure the flesh; and place a brand or a board under the bone to help cut the corrupted flesh; and you must continue treating as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and treat again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not appear, and the corruption is inside or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a brand underneath, and then treat the corruption from one part to the other, and let the treatment be the length of the corruption, a little, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and treat the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other way than to cut it; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand, or in the knuckle of the foot, then that is very difficult, but nonetheless, you must investigate the corrosion, how it appears to you; and clean it in all ways that you can, but be careful not to injure the veins or the nerves; and know that the tools and treatments for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore, you must prepare a tool for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the types of illnesses; so consider the tool you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder might rot due to internal causes or due to fire; and when you have medicated the rot with remedies and they do not work, then you must cut that limb to the place where the rot is, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the limb's failing; and the signs are that the limb turns black, so that it seems burned by fire, and after the blackness, rot; then this limb rot spreads to other limbs, and takes over the whole body; hurry to cut it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creature, like sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones, if the rot is in the fingertip, cut it, and do not give it time to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the rot does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no strong remedies are worth anything compared to its power; and do the same when the rot comes to the foot: if it is in the first joint, cut it after the other joint; and if it is in the foot, cut the entire foot; and if it goes up the leg, cut it at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the way to cut or treat the limb is to bandage it above and below, and have assistants pull one bandage down and the other up, and separate the flesh between the two bandages a small distance, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or treat it, and place a piece of linen on each side, so that the treatment does not touch the healthy area, and cause the patient further injury and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bandage the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed like a fire burn, and that rot came first to his toe, until it affected his whole foot; and when the man saw the rot, he quickly cut off the foot, and was healed; and a long time later, the rot returned to the finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repelling substances after cleaning his body, but the rot could not stop; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, for I had hope of repelling the matter; and I was also afraid that if I cut his hand, he might die, because the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and quickly cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have recounted this only so that one may do likewise, if one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy area, and remains so long that it collects a lot of pus; then it bursts and the pus escapes, and the area remains empty, like a vessel; and the skin on top is as thin as a thin cloth, and does not reach the bone, nor the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain," and not "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone deep down, it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is to cut the skin all around, especially when it is thin, like a cloth; and it does not worsen due to its rot.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you suspect the skin is inflamed and the rot is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with enemas as follows: examine if the swelling is large, and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then use an Egyptian medicine enema, made like this: take lead, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a pot over a fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take of it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and use it to rinse the wound, and draw the pus out; let the medicine remain there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the swelling is cleaned and the odor is gone; and sometimes it is rinsed with ash water, when this medicine is not available, and you take ashes of vine wood, pour water over it, then strain it, and use it as a rinse, until you know that the swelling is clean; and if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or ash water, use water and honey, or a little crushed litharge; or use honey and wine mixed, because the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine helps heal the wound; and when you have done this and you think the wound is cleaned, rinse it with what encourages the growth of flesh, such as a diafinit plaster mixed with rose oil and wine; or rinse it with medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned when discussing ointments; and if the wound opening is small, and the enema pipe cannot enter, widen it slightly with an iron tool, and place a compress of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, close it, leaving only the space where the enema can enter, and if the wound that expels pus is on top, cut it or move the incision to a lower place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the wound opening as you wish, arrange it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point, for when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow, and if you cannot cut the wound opening as you wish, arrange it in this way: so that the pus flows easily down and leaves no pus behind; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then cut the wound opening slightly wider than before, then apply a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the wound opening to push the pus out, and do not remove the large cloth except after several days; and the one over the wound opening is removed often to remove the pus, and observe if the pus is venom or little or enough, digested or indigested; and be aware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is applied in this way and you see nature rising up to the wound opening, know that the wound is healing and approaching health; and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the wound discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the wound will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom flows after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds take a long time to heal, and others whose wounds heal quickly; and if undigested pus comes out of the wound after many days, know that the wound will not heal; and if the wound is slow to heal and is inflamed, add drying medicines, both moist in substance and dry in effect, such as diafinit ointment, for it contains a significant amount of vitriol, and it is the last resort; take diafinit ointment, and mix it with rose oil and sprinkle some old wine, equal in substance; then mix it well and use it; and the same can be done with honey, cooked in strength, if diafinit ointment is not available, or you can take myrrh, aloes, and frankincense, and crush them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire; then stick it to a cloth and apply it to the wound, and sometimes an experienced physician uses long aristolochia, and roots of the heavenly lily, which is like the flour of chickpeas and centaury; and use it in simple or compound forms: grind them and make a powder, and place it on the honey I mentioned and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption has gone deep and has affected the bone, or hard parts, or ligaments; treat it with the fistula treatment, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A whitlow is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or perhaps on other fingers; and when it grows old and is not treated, a hard abscess develops, and it bursts and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps even destroys the entire nail; and the infection reaches the bone, causing foul pain, and the finger swells, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the section, and the treatment is ineffective, you must cut away all the remaining nail tissue with a sharp knife, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; but if the nail presses on the flesh, beginning to prick and wound it, you must lift the nail from the flesh that it is pricking, and push it upwards, and carefully and gently cut the flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove all of it; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the infection has reached the bone, you must cut it, and remove it forcefully, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger becoming corrupted, cut it in sections as previously described, and then treat it until it is healed; and if it is injured, pushed out, and causes great pain, you must first restore it to its proper place. Then cut the nail with a sharp, slightly slanted knife, ensuring the cut does not touch the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would experience extreme pain; and if it does happen, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand's finger.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The extra fingers that sometimes grow on some men's hands are sometimes completely fleshy, and sometimes have bones, and sometimes have nails, and some of them grow at the base of the joint, or the growth is in some of the finger's sections.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that grow in the middle of a finger don't change, and those that grow at the finger joint may change; the way to remove the fleshy one is straightforward: cut it at its root with a wide knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the base of the joint are difficult to treat: be cautious about cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those that grow at the back of the finger, you must first round off the flesh down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that occurs between the fingers comes from growth, or from wound healing, or from fire burns, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut the swelling so that the fingers return to their natural shape; then place between them soaked bandages or cloths in rose oil, to prevent them from fusing; or you place between them thin pieces of lead, until the area is healed as is proper.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs between any finger and the palm, cut the swelling as is appropriate.
des vils	of the vile ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large, swollen, and filled with melancholy superfluities, which appear in many parts of the body; and they occur more frequently in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you should administer a purge of bile, and afterwards, treat with a basil remedy.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is to cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein and draw out all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure is as follows: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the thick blood is thinned, then bind the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, or two, or three places, with a wide incision; then lift and draw the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows as the patient's strength can endure; then bind it up, and tell him to eat foods causing black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the blood is done in this way: shave the patient's leg if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over a fire, and then cut it along the vein from the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with a lancet, and scrape the vein from each side until it is visible when touched; and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord; then put the scraper underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then hang it with a light lancet, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the scraper, as you did before, and hang it with another lancet, as you did before; then make another incision, or several if you need to, then lift and cut at the toe, then draw and lift up to the second incision; then draw it from incision to incision, until all is drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, then put a needle with a strong double thread, and tie it and draw it, and put a scraper underneath, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, for if you cut it, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it will harm the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted, twisted, and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it gently, but do not cut it; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut straight, so as not to cut the vein; and it is of a large curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land; and perhaps it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the rot that comes beneath the skin, just as it comes within the body of snakes and worms, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes upon the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head is visible, you must wrap around a piece of lead of one and a half to two ounces, and a bandage, and leave the lead hanging on the leg, and every time it exits a little at the end, you wrap it around the lead and the bandage.  And if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at its root until it has all come out; for if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, and cause an abscess and rot in that place, and a bad illness.  Therefore, it must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body.  And sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long, or ten, and a man came to me once, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, you put a reed or a tube and pierce it to the bottom, so that it all comes out.  And the matter inside should be emptied, and healing medicines should be applied to the place to prevent any rot for some time, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or on the foot, and many holes come out from which blood spurts; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called "ox's disease" in our land, because it happens often to oxen, and is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it well by the movement from limb to limb, until it pierces the skin where it goes, and bursts out. And it is caused by the corruption of certain humors, like worms, serpents, and leeches, and ascarides in the belly.  One fears its harm, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head and the eye, it may re-enter and destroy the eye, and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you wish to treat and extract it, one can only do it when it is visible:  therefore, you must bind the area above and below with a strong bandage, tightly, then cut above it and pull it out.  And if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it, you cauterize it with fire above it until it is cooked/ripened.  And the greatest harm it causes is that it can affect the eye, as we said; and if you see it approaching the head near the eye, you must firmly press the eyebrow underneath it, then cut above it, and pull it out.  And the patient must use body cleansers and remedies that dissolve the corrupting bad humors, and abstain from foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from wind/flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have witnessed this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it ascend like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like liquid silver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that place and settled into the shoulder, and then a bit later ran throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it would repeatedly circle around the body, as I saw it.
