Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from limb to limb in this way, for I had never seen this illness according to this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many where pain had moved from one place to another, but I had never seen it like I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and exposed veins, and for that reason the flatulence seemed constrained; and it does not appear according to this reasoning in those who are fleshy, and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then lance it above and below hastily, and then cut until that constrained flatulence in the place is released; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with things that expel flatulence, such as foul-smelling pills, and scarlet pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points, and small, and barbed, and soldered; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that strikes any limb strikes in two ways: either in a principal limb it pierces, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes, then, in any of these limb locations, and the signs of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you: you must refrain from extracting this arrow, for death follows in many cases; and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and the surface tissue over the brain is torn, is when there is blindness, swelling, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is a discharge of fluid from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and white, dusty matter oozes from the wound, as well as burned flesh; and if these signs appear, refrain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is when it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were lodged in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat appear, and fainting: then know without doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow striking the lung is that frothy blood flows from the wound, the throat swells, the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks coolness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the chest wall, it is near the ribs; and it causes great pain and sighs; and all the shoulder muscles move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps some undigested food matter oozes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and some straw spurts out through the intestines, there is no hope of cure, nor of arrow extraction.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine spurts out and comes forth, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, shoulder joint, spine of the back, arms, thighs, and legs, and similar limbs, are saved according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is lodged in a nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you will do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of his nose: I tried it, and pulled it out from the other side beneath the fat of his ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that struck him in the fat of his eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and I could only grasp the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, like all light iron without ears; the man was healed, and no bad accident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab with ears: I shaved the beard, and I worked so hard that I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled an arrow from a man, which had lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die; and then after thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut around the arrow, and I widened the wound, and I pulled it out, and he had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I saw a man whose arrow lodged in his back, and the wound was closed over; and the arrow remained inside him, and he did not change his natural dispositions, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, whom an arrow struck in his face, and the wound closed; and it remained like that without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I pulled an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had lodged in the middle of his nose, and was slightly slanted to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat him after it had lodged there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a very fine probe, and felt nothing; and he felt a prickling and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the area so that it would not swell, and the arrowhead's location became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained like this for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose one day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a sharp, corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open, and probed it, and felt the arrowhead protruding from the area; then I added the sharp medicine to the opening of the wound, until the arrowhead appeared visibly; and the period of treatment extended over four months, and then the wound widened so that I could insert the forceps, and moved it back and forth, but it would not come out. Then I did not cease to refine and devise ways with instruments, until I found a pair of well-crafted forceps, as will be described at the end of this chapter, with which I extracted it, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:  I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the qualities of extracting some arrows, so that you apply your treatment to what I haven't said, for the book cannot encompass everything; but the wise master, considering a small thing, and what is present and lacking, finds new work and new instruments, in response to the unusual occurrences that arise in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs where they are lodged except in two ways: either through the place where they entered, or through another part; and the one that emerges through the place it entered, is an arrow that entered fleshy parts, and sometimes emerges immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not emerge immediately, leave it until the flesh around it is softened and the exit is eased; and if it is lodged in the bone and cannot emerge, leave it thus for several days and move it each day; and then it will emerge; and if it does not, pierce around it with a very fine drill, until the area around it is widened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the symptoms I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not extract it, but leave it until it is equalized after some days, for if the arrow reaches this point, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone, and does not reach the surface, and the patient survives several days without adverse symptoms, then consider extracting it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot emerge, apply drills around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged inside the body, so that it cannot be seen, search for it thoroughly; and if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, widen the wound until it is large; and extract the arrow if you can; and if the arrow has ears with which it is lodged, remove the flesh which is embedded from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can extract it; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, so that you do not extract it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you hesitant, apply what we have said about treatment in this chapter; and be wary of cutting the nerve and the vein, and devise how you can safely extract the arrow, quickly or slowly, forcefully or gently; and position the patient as he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help, and if you cannot, position him according to the signs they show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes out from another side, or from which something is apparent, or the skin is swollen on the spot so that it can be seen or felt clearly, then cut above it, so that the pliers can grip it, and then extract it; it will come out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, rotate your hand smoothly until it enters the bone and widens the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, remove the entire shaft; and if the shaft is broken, and you want to administer a thrust, administer the pointed instrument, so that the arrowhead enters the instrument's groove; and then thrust forcefully, and if the arrowhead is broken, apply an instrument with a pointed end that penetrates it, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is poisoned, you must cut all the surrounding flesh where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrowhead pierces the groin, or the belly, or the bladder, or the ribs, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, cut there; and be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead's shaft is also like a bird's feather, to fit the tip of the arrow, as is this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and grasping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which blood can be drawn, of which sixteen are in the head:  Two beating ones behind the ears, called the two "herbech"; and two arteries that are in the two visible temples; and two veins in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the tip of the nose; and the two "guindeges" that are in the neck; and two veins that are in the upper lips, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly drawn from are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is above the bend, and is the one from which one draws blood, which is clearly visible on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the auricular and annular, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is beneath the bend of the ankle on the left side, and the second is the "sophene" that is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Bleeding from the veins behind the ears helps with chronic colds and headaches; and the method of drawing blood, as I tell you, is to raise the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the patient tighten their neck with a bandage, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places on the head; grasp them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, gently make a mark; then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to raise the whole vein upward, and cut both the skin and the vein with two finger-lengths of the blade, and release blood as desired; then compress and bind, until it is healed; and I have already described the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Bleeding from the two arteries in the temples is good for chronic, severe headaches, and habitual eye inflammation, and for acute eye tears; and the method of bleeding is as I say: and is that the patient tightens their neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, and then make a mark; then lift the part above the vein up with your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and raise the vein upwards, and cut it, as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as effective as bleeding from the cephalic vein for chronic facial illnesses, headaches, and redness; and the method is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument called a "fossor", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and strike it with your hand, or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity you desire; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed, and sometimes use a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the bandage should not be too sharp; and bleed transversely, because the bone is close, and the bandage might break if it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Bleeding from the two veins that are in the temples helps with eye problems, and inflammation, and redness, and eye infections, and facial illnesses; and the method for bleeding them is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting in some way, as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be transverse, with a bandage that is a little long and a little wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is thin, it might break; then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then bind with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding from the vein in the nose is good for fevers, and severe madness, and facial illnesses, such as headaches and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is long-standing; and the method for bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck, then grasps their nose with your left hand, and take a thin long bandage, and place it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein is not clearly visible there, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your needs, and then bind it for a night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the bandage:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Bleeding from the two temples helps with constriction of the throat, and the beginning of a rash, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and sores, and herpes, and boils; and the method for bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck from both sides, as we have said; and let the master stand above the patient's head, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein lengthwise a little wide, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then do the same to the other vein, then untie the bandage, and moderately tighten both veins, so the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, so the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins on the upper lips helps with cold sores in the mouth, and the corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips and nose and around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the method for bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you, and tighten their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look for two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized because they are dark, and because there are small dark veins around them: then cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding from the veins below the tongue helps after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for ailments of the eye, and for ailments of the mouth; and the method of bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and you lift their tongue, and look for a dark vein on each side below it: then bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, because the arteries are below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm, which are commonly bled, are bled in two ways: either by piercing with a wide, flat lancet, or a narrow, pointed one, like a sharp knife, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide or narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flat lancet is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And is needed to open veins filled with thick, visible blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood; and that is the shape of the pointed lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for bleeding thin veins, where there is thin, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps ailments located under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed wisely, and to be wary of the artery which is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it must be stopped, as I have said; and the lancet must not be pointed, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein is not clearly visible, you must press it and change to another; or you seek out a branch of it, or you bleed the vein in the middle of the arm: it will be clearly visible; and cut it with the knife-shaped lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the site for the bleeding, it is necessary first that you press the arm, that you touch the site until you know the pulse; then mark the site with a mark, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the knife-shaped lancet; and be careful that you do not injure the artery when you see the site inflamed, for it is of the artery; then stop it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see blood gushing out like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it like that, and do not move it, the patient; and let him be cautious, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overwhelms you, and the physician is not present, then cut the artery if it is visible, for the head of it will retract; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a fig-tree bark, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind over well until the other day; if the blood stops, it is good; if not, then treat it, as we have said, with the powders that stop blood; and the stopping of it is not serious in many cases because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the vein in the middle helps to draw blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the leech that it passes by the nerve that is below, and if it penetrates too deeply, and it finds the nerve, and it swells and the health is serious, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve appears very often, and if it does not appear in any man because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you bleed it with the instrument; and protect the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by pricking at the olive-colored or myrtle-colored vein, because it is the safest of all the veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to look for the easiest place, and nothing is harmed if one fails the first time, and one starts again; and perhaps the place swells in some people when one fails the first time, but nothing is harmed.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not administered except to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are on the elbow: that is to say, cephalic, basilic, and median cubital; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding administered for illnesses has no set time, but whenever necessary, by day or by night, at all hours and at all times; and it is not appropriate to bleed children until fourteen years of age, nor women who are pregnant except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle clyster if they have retained much waste, so that the veins do not draw impurities from the intestines that harm the principal limbs; nor should those who are overly full of food, or drunk, be bled, as long as they are still affected; nor the hydrops; and one should refrain from bleeding after a colic attack, vomiting, or diarrhea, and multiple sexual encounters, and hard labor, sleepless nights and fasting, and anything that depletes all strength, either from the spirit or the body; then subtilize the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and remedies, if you are able; then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein on the inner arm near the elbow, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, hardship, lust, and similar things; and be relaxed and cheerful; and let the bleeder be taller than the one being bled; and the bleeder should rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, because if it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow; and then the bleeder should rub the area with their hands, until the veins swell and are palpable; then the bleeder should moisten the lancet with a bit of old oil, then place their left hand's finger over the vein below the bleeding point, so that the vein does not burst or fail when the lancet is introduced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like ropes when bleeding, and there are those that are full of wind, so that when the lancet is applied, it retracts and the vein will not open, and so it is with these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for this reason, it is necessary that the bleeder be careful in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, he must try again a little below or above that spot, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let it rest for a day or two, and do not bandage the arm; perhaps a hot abscess will result. Do not enter a bath, then recommence the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or if the blood flows subtly, and you fear it will not bleed as much as you desire, then thrust the lancet directly into the same opening; and open it slightly above, before the area swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not recommence the bleeding, but apply a little oil plaster, for it alleviates the body's blood and the plaster is gentler in this area than oil; and thus administer oil plaster in every bleeding you do to the veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and this same thing does the white clay and the powder, when applied to the area; it subtilizes the blood and thins it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess develops, which happens often, especially when the vein is not bled vigorously the first time or the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and apply a sponge soaked in warm water and salt to the area, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flows from the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains in the area after a few days, it does not harm him; and if you wish, apply something of aloes or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mandrake, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscess and bad appearance occur after vein bleeding: put your hand over it, and if you find the area soft upon pressing your hand, this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then do not apply any of the things we have mentioned, for perhaps arterial blood will flow; but apply a dry plaster to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out each blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is strong and needs bloodletting that a larger wound be made, with wide incisions; and for the weak, do the opposite, and bleed them little and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking; and this way of bleeding avoids the outflow of blood and severing of nerves, and is better than bleeding from the long or wide veins.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for someone whose body weakens during bloodletting, give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, bleed them three or four times.  And if they are of a cold temperament, give them bread soaked in rose-water syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup, before the bloodletting.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if they faint during bloodletting, after the release of much blood, it is necessary that they sip broth made from meat, and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things we have described in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to vent his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by a great bleeding, that he be bled little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to vent their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, should bleed them seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another part, should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body, which is already heated and causes fever; therefore, a large quantity must be drawn, and the opening widened until it bleeds profusely; then you must observe all the conditions of bloodletting, and place your hand over their pulse while they bleed, so death does not come instead of fainting, and this happens many times when the bloodletter is negligent; and it is not right when you want to untie the arm and make blood issue the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press forcefully; nor if it is bent, that they extend their arm hastily, for that would be bad; but let it be until it bleeds a second time; or you prick it with the tip of the flame, so that the blood that is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out strongly, and place a little salt dissolved in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a necessity to draw blood a second time, bleed them in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein at the head because it is better composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until the skin is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein is clearly visible, then bleed through the center, not wide or long; and the opening should be wide, and bleed close to the joint of the hand; and if blood cannot flow, place the hand back in warm water, and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, because it is used more in winter than in summer; and bloodletting from this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein on the back of the right hand is good for all liver ailments, and this is the method: squeeze the hand and put it in warm water until the vein swells, so that it can be seen; and if you bleed across, and if you cut it completely, nothing will be harmed; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all the exposed flesh; and then return the hand to warm water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot flow.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as you need, apply oil and resin to the vein to close it quickly, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the vein in the left hand is good for mouse disease, and do as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bloodletting from the saphena vein is good for all ailments below the body, such as illnesses of the spleen, retention of urine, kidney and thigh and leg ailments, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the method for this bloodletting is that the patient puts their foot in warm water and rubs the vein until it swells, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and many veins run from above the foot; therefore, bleed at the widest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed above the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and bleed through it as if cutting; and let the fire be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood will not come out, put the foot back in the water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the lancing fails the first time, start again a little higher, for the spot is often sore; but be mindful of the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise with the saphena on the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its bleeding is good for hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the method for its bleeding is that the patient enters a bath, and tightens above the ankle with four fingers by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not appear; and if it appears, bleed it in all the ways you can, and by piercing it; and it is better that you cut it, for the spot is safe, and it is very responsive to hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot find it, bleed any visible vein on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and allow as much blood to flow as you wish, then loosen the bandage, and apply cotton and press it; it is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horn, or bronze, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without striking is in two ways: either with fire, or without fire; and cupping done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is on the top of the head; and another in the middle of the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and the cup under the chin; and the cups on the two shoulders; and the cups above the hips; and the cups between the two arms; and the cups on the two legs; and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore does not weaken the person as with a vein's bleeding; and it should not be applied, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if cupping is needed for illnesses, or for custom, it should be applied each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have the tongue swollen, and spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we instruct them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	Bleeding from the temple helps the heaviness of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it should not be used by those of cold complexion, or those who have a cold, for it does them great harm; and therefore it should not be used by the elderly, nor those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed from it become forgetful, and therefore the cup should be placed a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping in the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilica vein, and therefore it is useful for tightening of the breast, and for splitting of the bronchial tube, and for coughs, and for fullness; and it should be applied gently, for if it holds too tightly, it causes forgetfulness in the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, eye strain and migraines, and for strangulation, and for toothache, and it is in place of bleeding from the basilica vein; and you should instruct the practitioner to press his hand gently when applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and there is no excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth diseases, and for gum corruption, and similar ailments of the mouth; and it is in place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for illnesses caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as effective as bleeding from the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the practitioner not to press too deeply, for the area is lacking in flesh, and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	Cupping on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for ailments beneath, and the cup should be large, and made of bronze, as it needs to draw well; and perhaps if it were delicate, it would break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping on the legs draws blood openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for longstanding pains in the kidneys, and the bladder, and relieve the swellings; and they are in place of the two shins, and the two ankles, and nonetheless they weaken the body after prolonged use, and cause paleness in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cupping is to first make it empty, and then suck gently, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing so until you see the area become red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then stop, and replace the cupping, and be mindful of the body's condition, for there are those who have thick flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to make the path of the thick blood thinner.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw little blood gradually, one strike is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we begin again often; and if the blood is thick, strike deep into it, and the end result is that the skin is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, to oil the areas of the cups with an aperitive and dissolving oil: if it is summertime, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if it is wintertime, withcress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take amarant oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being bled has tender skin and large pores, no oil should be put on, but it should be washed after the cupping with rose water, or cold water, or blackberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise with basil, or myrtle water, or sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities rise with old wine, or oak water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not bleed with a cupping before bathing or while bathing, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after cupping, and one must be careful, when one is about to be cupped and when one is cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be careful if the one being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; they should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce with basil, and similar things; and eat little, and the flesh of a hare, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and medium-bodied fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat little, and eat small birds and pigeons; and the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping, to strengthen the main limbs; and if the blood is thin, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping that is placed without striking is placed on the liver, on the spleen, gout, and on the belly, the gut, kidneys, and hip, because these limbs do not tolerate being struck on them, and one does it only to draw blood from one limb to another, as we place them on the breasts when a nipple bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place cupping on the belly and gut to lessen the limb; and it relieves the pain, when there is a blockage or stone, it removes, by its attractive virtue, perhaps the blockage or moves the stone from its place; and this is how it works when one places it on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these cuppings are administered empty just to suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with lukewarm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the cupping with hot water alone, or water in which one has cooked suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have one small hole in the side near the middle, just large enough to insert a needle, and be made of bronze, smooth enough so it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and have a crossbar of bronze or iron in the middle to hold a lit candle, and there should be large and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who use them; because the cuppings for children are different from those for the old, and the thin ones different from the fat ones.
