Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping on the limb like this: take the candle made of wax or linen, and place it in the middle of the cupping, through the rod in the middle of the cupping, so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping, so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the hole we have mentioned, so that when one wants, the vapor escapes, and one removes the cupping; and one picks up the linen like before, and one repeats it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping, then, which is administered in a pleurisy, with water only, there is no rod nor hole, and it is only administered when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb simply; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only administered to limbs where cuppings cannot be applied because of their small size, like the lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, like the toes or nails, and others similar; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in clean fresh water without any injury, take them; and put them in fresh water for a night, until they are full, and have nothing in their bellies; and then, having been bled from a vein and a cupping, rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cupping can be applied, place one there, because that is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, remove the place of the wound, then water, well, and then dry it; and if the wound heals too quickly after the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and apply it, until the blood is drawn out; and if the blood is excessive, place ground vitriol or gallstones, and similar things, until it is drawn out; or you place half of peeled beans on the place, and leave them until they get hot, so it will stop now; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not want to take hold, rub the place with fresh blood, or you prick it with a needle until blood comes out, and then place them on, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will become attached; and when you see them falling off, sprinkle some powdered alum and salt or ashes on them, and they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, my dear son, that many fools disdain this chapter, as if they had never seen any of the ancient books, nor read any letters; and for this reason, knowledge is rare in our land, for I have never found any good one. I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have mastered the subject, and through experience and the practice of my life. I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in the two chapters before this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, therefore, that in the prologue of this book we state the sum of the subject and the chapters where the wise man focuses his understanding and remains true, so that those who practice this skill may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twisting, or crushing occurs to someone, you must quickly bleed the patient on both sides, if nothing else hinders you, such as weakness of the body, or if they are a child or an old person, or if the weather is not too hot or too cold; and avoid eating cold meats, namely cold joints, and the flesh of birds and hares, and let them not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill them with foods that cause blood to accumulate in the veins, lest you fear a hot abscess or the spread of matter to the limb; so that the patient returns to the prior state of health which he previously used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient foods that promote healthy growth, where they have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and turnips, and feet, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the fracture heals more quickly and more completely.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal or mend properly according to their nature because of the dryness of their limbs, nor those of the very young, such as the bones of small children.  However, there is a cure; apply strong bandages which hold and join the limb together, until it is as strong as it was before.  And this work does not heal completely, and therefore it is necessary to nourish them with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that run along, and others that are jagged, like the edge of a writing pen.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with a wound, and fractures with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type there is its own method and appropriate instrument in restoration, according to what the memory returns to its place; and the fracture of the bone is recognized by its twisted position, and is clearly seen by its deformity, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture; but there may be twisting, or a crack, or a minor fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move it by hand, but apply the following medicines, and then gently restrain it.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that a fracture that runs along, and the two parts are separated, you must now put them in equal alignment, lest a hot abscess come; and if a hot abscess comes, leave it for a day or so, until the abscess subsides; then put it in alignment as gently and wisely as you can, and know that restoration is easier than in cases with pieces; then restrain it as is appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if it is a hand or foot, or with your hand if it's a small limb, or with two cords, or with a cord and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, realign all the additions to their places as gently as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain; and properly join the two ends of the bones according to the best possible forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not properly aligned: then straighten it beautifully, and do not restrain it too tightly, nor press it as those who, through their work, cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is aligned, carefully instruct the patient not to move it, neither when awake nor when asleep, nor turning, nor in any other way; and carefully ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly aligned, and it must be put into such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed straight, that no twisting occurs once it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar ones: so it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: so it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb, and bind it equally on all sides, so that there is no unevenness; then tie around light padding, three or four turns depending on the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten it less, so that the fracture then moves the fracture slightly; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and turn it around the fracture area again; then return to the area below the fracture and tighten it moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we said in the first book above; then put linen padding or cloths between the bandages, until it is all even, then tie everything over a bandage, and then place your well-made splints over it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something on top that calms the abscess and removes the swelling, and leave it thus for a few days; then bandage over your splints, and let them be half the width of a cleverly cut cane, or of wood from which clefts are made, or of palm stalks, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint placed over the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large; then bandage over the splints as you did in the first book, then tie over a thread evenly, as in the first book over the fracture; tighter on top, then looser; and the thread must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages from twisted linen cords, and that is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not necessary that there be less than a finger's width of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the ends of the splints after tightening in healthy places, put linen padding or wool wadding under them so that he is not injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to tighten splints on all fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put splints on it until after 5 or 7 days, or more, according to your certainty of a hot abscess occurring; and see here the method of ancient poultices for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains: take flour that remains on the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of poultice for restoring a fracture in many cases, especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains: take 3 parts of asafoetida, and pennyroyal, and enula, and saffron, and gum arabic, and mugwort, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 5 grams; 9 grams of aloeswood; and make it into a powder, and mix it with plenty of egg; if the person's constitution is hot, use this poultice, for it is a good compound and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another poultice that is good for sprains: take mugwort and marshmallow, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 9 grams; acacia 6 grams; Armenian bole 10 grams, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another poultice for dislocated joints and separated bones, which eases the resulting pain, and promotes healing of the bone and the fracture: take new wool, soak it in oil and cooked oil, and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These poultices do not restore, but they are good for calming a hot abscess, and they properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another poultice that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of ground poppy, and grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another poultice for the restoration of a broken bone and for diminishing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and chickpea flour, each in equal parts; grind them, and mix with wine; if the limb is inflamed, mix with moist coriander water or water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another, stronger poultice than the first, when a hard abscess occurs to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mallow, flaxseed, balm, melilot, and plantain, and violet and chamomile flowers, equal parts of each; grind them, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should only apply to a broken limb, to restore strength, a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should apply to a broken limb, for restoration, somewhat dry and warm things, like myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar things, as we have stated.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another poultice that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped horsehair, or bird feathers, and mallow, and willow bark, equal parts; grind them, and make a poultice and bind it on.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, after a while, remove it and see if the patient feels no pain, and that the bone has not shifted from its place.  If not, do not remove it for several days. And if pain, itching, lack of rest, or swelling appear in the area, hurry, remove the poultice immediately, and take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and immerse it in water and apply it to the area until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place dry wool, soaked in rose water or oil, and bandage it for a night, until you are sure there is no hot abscess.  And relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the thin bandage, with a little poultice, and don't bind it as tightly as before.  Continue this until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling are completely gone, and you need a poultice and bandage, start again in the same way you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, do not remove the bandage until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the fracture heals and the flesh approaches; then tighten it more than before, and increase the nourishment, as I said before; and if you see the area drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it.  Then moisten it with warm water, every time you remove the bandage, and every third day, loosen the bandage slightly.  By this work, the nourishment to the limb is hastened, and it is better than the wrong methods of the foolish surgeons who reattach the limb incorrectly.  This is bad, and it is dangerous work.  I see no other way than to leave it alone and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many types of fractures exist, with diverse forms and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by a sword blow, and the collarbone breaks all the way down to the cartilage beneath the bone, just as a hatchet or stick does.  For this reason, this type of fracture is called "hatching.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone from above, piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "complete"; and the wound from these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt impact, or a fissure, or a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there are wounds that penetrate the bone as subtly as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and forces a piece of the bone inward, and the place is splintered as blacksmiths do when they strike on cauldrons; thus, the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have soft bones in their head, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated from them like splinters; and I will talk about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures through their separation, and by the investigation of the tissues, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary-like fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is uncovered, and one rubs against it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, watch out for the patient's complications, and if you see any bad complications, such as vomiting of phlegm, loss of understanding, stretching, paleness, acute fever, and the eyes becoming inflamed and red, and other similar symptoms in many situations, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any frightening complications, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the tissue under the bone be corrupted, and the complications we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, you must split the broken part like this:  take the head of the wounded patient and uncover the bone in every way you can, and gently on the surface of the wound, and if a discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, or a festered abscess, help with what is necessary.  Fill the space with cloths soaked in rose oil, and let the wound rest until the festered abscess is calmed and you are sure there is no more blood discharge.  Then start removing the bone, using one of two methods: the first method is to cut closely around it, and this is the shape...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is to use several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of tempered iron; and work carefully, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, you must pierce around it before making cuts with drills.  Do not drill so deeply that the point pierces through the bone of the skull.  Each drill point should have a rim or circle around the point that prevents the point from going through the bone.  You will need several such drills, each placed in the thickness of the bone so that each one can drill through to the bone.  And this is the shape of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The method for piercing around the fractured bone is to place a drill on the bone and rotate it with your fingers until you know the bone is pierced.  Then reposition the drill a short distance away and do the same all around.  Then use incisors to cut the bone in between the holes, as subtly and gently as possible, until you extract the bone with your hand, or with any tools you have like pliers or tweezers.  Be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, you must remove any remaining fragments of bone with a tool similar to an incisor, but thinner and more delicate than the other incisor.  If any small bone fragments or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the tools. Then treat the wound with the dressings and ointments we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen described, which is safer; and he highly praises it, and this is his statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a portion of the bone, where the fracture is visible.  Once you have exposed that part, place the head of this lens-shaped incisor underneath the area, and this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only; its edge is sharp on two sides, so the cutting edge is towards the bone.  Then strike gently with a small mallet, cutting the bone all around, and be very careful of the tissue underneath.  If it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the tissue, and the bone is only broken on the surface, and there are small pieces, you must remove the rough edges and take off the scales with the fine rasp, of which you should have various sizes, to best apply in each area, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use larger rasps first, and then finer ones afterwards, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other cuts and subtle fractures, you must use an appropriate method according to its direction; and this is something that is not readily understood by those who have not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the surface is exposed, you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil.  Place it over the wound.  Then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth.  Do this as gently as possible so you don't press on the surface.  Then apply another bandage, but don't tighten it too much, only enough to hold the wound.  Leave it on for one or two days, until the inflamed abscess is calmed.  Then remove it and apply remedies such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things.  Mix these into a powder and apply to the wound.  Apply these medicines frequently without causing irritation.  Keep the wound clean, and do not allow any ointment to remain or any pus to collect.  For when pus gathers on the tissue of the brain, it will spread and fester, causing the patient great harm.  Because when you put something irritating on the surface, it will cause further injury.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be careful, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the darkening isn't severe except for the medicine applied, meaning it has that effect, you should take a portion of honey and three portions of rose oil, and apply it to a cloth, and place it over the surface.  Then treat it in the necessary ways until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the nose are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should place your index finger in the nostril and align the broken part against your index finger, and the other by the outside, so that the nose returns to its natural shape.  Do this gently and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, you should align it with the head of a small, somewhat thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, do likewise, and hurry to restore it on the first day if possible; otherwise, after the seventh or tenth, when the painful abscess has subsided, then place linen strips on the tip of the nose if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place one on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that the strips should be soaked in butter and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they should be soaked in a mixture of egg white and powdered flour; then leave the strip until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose instead of strips, and a soft cloth is wrapped around, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes through it; now do what you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil comes to the nose while you are working on it, place a plaster or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a little bit of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil does not come, apply a plaster on the outside, made of cumin flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then place light bandages over it, and do not bind the nose; and if the nasal fracture is small, and it is broken into small pieces, remove it with suitable instruments, then sew the fissure, and treat it with things that unite flesh and bind, like suitable plasters and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with strips and place lead strips on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken from the inside, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only external, and not broken into two, except for splinters inside, it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, put your right index finger in, and gently push the fracture inward, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension from two sides, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or breakage, tie them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place a bandage on the broken jaw, and place a double cloth over it; and place a large, well-made lead plate, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then restore what has changed; and apply a plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after you have removed the bandage; and put light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster holds, and the patient's condition doesn't change, leave it until they are healed; many times they are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, check if any piece of bone has been removed; if so, try to remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, stitch the wound if it is large, and apply appropriate plasters to promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps often break before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is, when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the broken forceps is; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then align the fracture with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round pad of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and it should be large according to your needs; and extend and lift the forceps, and grasp the pad in your hand, so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps out, because it goes deep inside, it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and the assistants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the forceps is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, you must cut it open; and pull the pieces slightly, and if the bone cannot join by any means, cut it with one of the scalpels you have; but be sure to place this instrument under the forceps to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, but is not sharp, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two ends, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound you made when you separated the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the opening is small, or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, soak a bandage in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of the bone, when there are no wounds or cuts, is to place on the bone a plaster of mill powder and egg white, and put light bandages on top, and place a splint underneath the armpit if you need it; then take a very wide bandage, one palm wide, and place a doubled bandage over the bandages, and the plaster; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and place the splint over the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy and diseased armpit; and move it from each side, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture together and you clearly see that the splint does not move over the broken bone, watch it daily, and when the ligament weakens, restrict it; and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the armpit while they sleep to raise the shoulder; this will ease the fracture of the shoulder by easing the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, for up to twenty days; then resume the plaster if you see that it is needed, and restrain and leave it like this until it is restored; and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and in less time in some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder breaks in a wide or middle place, and it is not known for certain except by touch; then adjust it according to the shape of the fracture and reposition it according to its natural form in every way possible; then put mill powder with egg white on the area, and light bandages, and place a doubled bandage over it; then put on a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are any bumps under the splint in any part of the shoulder, fill those bumps with linen bandages so that the splint is even; and then firmly bind it with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and examine the ligament daily; and every time it weakens, tighten it, and adjust the splint if it is off its place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty or twenty-five days.  And when this number is complete, untie it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that will easily be put out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and is under the skin, then cut open it and remove it, and do as we have said in the treatment of a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the hip
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The hip is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it shifts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of breath, and sickness, and perhaps vomits blood, and bumps appear in the broken bone, and one can feel them clearly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and place a cushion between their shoulders, then press on the shoulders, and bring the ribs of the two ribs together with your hands, and subtly try to make it even in all the ways you can, until the bone's shape is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the area, using a thin layer of salt, or another light material, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it over the broken bone so that it does not move; and wrap the bandage around the back, and tie it securely, and check the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, then tighten it; and if it needs to be undone, due to inflammation or itching that appears in the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and treat what has happened there in various ways; then reapply the plaster, and tie it tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs mostly occurs in the thick parts behind the back, and at the inside edge, and they bend only because they are fragile; and one can feel this well by examining the ribs.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you align the fracture, as is appropriate.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it tightly with a bandage, if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fractured ribs are angled inward, the patient feels extreme pain and piercing, like stabbing, because the bone pierces the tissue; and coughs with sharp pains, and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients devoted much effort to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that you should administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest a hot abscess arise, if one has not already developed.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if one has developed, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say that cupping should be placed on the area, to draw out strongly, and that seems reasonable; however, there is concern that the cupping may draw the superfluities to the area because of the weakness in its disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and that tents should be placed between the ribs to evenly bandage the surrounding area, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone piercing the skin, and the patient is in doubt, then it is necessary to cut open the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the surface; and then one must cut into the bone, and gently pull, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, then put cloths soaked in rose oil on it; and treat the area as is appropriate for an abscess, and let it lie often on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and it rarely bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then watch if you see their hands soft and swollen and lifeless, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, watch if their feet are soft, and if the accidents are there that are in their hands, and on the back there is a sudden wind and expulsion without will; and when they are placed on their stomach, there is sudden expulsion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when they are placed on their back and want to sit up, they cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal; do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not come to them, the condition is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you observe if there is a hot abscess, put rose oil or egg oil on the spine until it is calmed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone separates, it is necessary to cut above where it is; and remove the bone, then bring the two sides of the wound together, if it is large, with stitching, then treat it with a healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the thigh," place your left hand's fingertip there, and bring it equal to your other hand as much as you can, then place the plaster and the splint if you need it; then bind it, and if there is a detached bone, cut it open, and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Often it happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, there isn't much crumbling at the head; and it cracks lengthwise, and bends inward, and causes the patient pain in the area, and throbbing, and swelling of what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand over, until you are over the break; and understand what the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, bring that break to equal alignment, so that it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is lengthwise, or it bends inward, make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that break is ready for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it in alignment, put on the plaster, then place a splint of wood or a board, and bind the break tightly, so that it does not move; and fill the area beneath the ribs, so that the limb is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess comes, do not touch it, until the hot abscess is calmed, and apply what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the break of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the rib and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two methods: of which one is that you take a splint of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two bandages to the two ends, and hang them upwards, and seat the patient on a chair; then place the patient's broken arm on the splint, until it reaches the armpit, and have a bend in the splint, then hang it on some heavy object or the attendant extends it downwards; then the attendant aligns the fracture with their hands together, until the fracture returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on their back, and ties the hand to their neck, then instruct two attendants that one holds that which is above the fracture in their hands, and the other holds below with a bandage, and each extends to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the traction to be stronger, tie a bandage below the fracture, and above the fracture, and each of the attendants pulls in their direction.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you must place one bandage below the armpit, and another towards the rib, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the rib, you must lightly place a bandage there without effort, until the fracture is even on the spot and on the rib; then align the fracture as it should, and hold it if no boils appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if boils appear, do not hold it tight for seven days, and place soaked wool and rose oil, until the boils are soothed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you place the plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put the bandage, and pull on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one finger's width of space, and let each splint be so large that it extends three finger-widths from the fracture on either side; then hold tight on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, more firmly and less in length.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, at the time you reset the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the bandage every three days, to see that itching or swelling does not occur, or that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it aligns, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their hands on their stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion full of wool as well, and check every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the bandages are not softened; correct it by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is first subtle; and when it begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.
