And when the dislocation is outward, the patient lies as we said for those with hip problems, and tightens a strap around the sick leg properly, and around the foot also; then put two splints, one at the top and one at the feet, then place one splint between the patient's thighs in the middle; and let them be covered with damp cloths around so that they do not injure the patient, then let each assistant pull towards themselves, and the attending physician should place the dislocation equally with their hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, and press it as we said for hip problems, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly extend the sick leg, as I have said; and the attending physician should put their effort on the afflicted part, then press with the other hand and extend it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is outward, it is not necessary to extend the patient downwards or lift them from the ground, but it must be as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we said concerning the lying on two hips; and let them lie on their side, and the strap is stretched as we said before, and one must press on the joint with the table; and it will be in place when the patient extends their legs, and they are even; then close the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind them with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and place the plaster over it; and if you see that they are even, bind it, as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind it, and let the limb move gently, until the member is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward, outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not fit against their thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their side, and place their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and draw it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and another attendant extends their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they fit their leg against their thigh easily; and place a plaster over it, and make the leg fit against the thigh, and bind them tightly together for three or four days, then unbind them; and the patient must not walk, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes moved, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it protrudes on the side where it is dislocated: the repositioning is gentle, and it should be gently pulled by the hands when it is only moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and two assistants hold the leg firmly above the ankle; then pull the foot towards your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and gently push the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, start the work again, for it returns; and if it cannot return thus, have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a strong staff firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around it so it doesn't injure the patient; then one assistant holds the thigh, and another assistant extends the foot with their hands or with a rope, which they tie to the back of the foot; then each assistant pulls equally, and the staff should be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient while they are being extended; then the assistants reposition the dislocation with their hands, and another assistant holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is properly positioned, apply the plaster and bandages, bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and be careful of the tendons above the ankle, that the bandages are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if boils arise there, you must treat them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, they must be gently extended without difficulty, and it is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, you must have the patient sit on a flat surface, or a table, upright, place your foot on the exposed joints, then press firmly on it until it returns; and when it is aligned and nothing is protruding, place a plank under the sole of the foot, about two inches wide, and bind it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies:  be not presumptuous in the treatment unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and be compassionate and merciful and slow, not rash; and at the beginning use soothing poultices for the abscess, and leave the patient to God's will if you see no hope of health; and when you do see hope, then reposition the limb immediately, before the hot abscess gets there; and when the limb is in place, apply soothing poultices for the abscess and treat the wound as is necessary with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones separated, then remove them, and do as we said in simple maladies; and guard against entering a path of fear, as I said, for this will alter you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your skill and your body.
Amen	Amen
